Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it by the ancients "cure contuse", and you should make three equal incisions on the forehead of the patient who has this illness, according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the incisions be as deep as two doins running down from above until the nose, and the other two at the sides above the sinews, and beware not to incise the arteries that are at the sides above the sinews; and keep your hand away from the continuity of the lower jaws, and let each wound be the size of three doins through; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much linen to wipe off the blood, then apply sharp spatumile from both sides as it is made.
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is from the temple to the second incision; and brandish all the cheek which is over the sinew above the bone, then do the same from the middle incision until the other second one, and then withdraw firmly this spatumile.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you insert into the first cut the instrument called "cultellaire", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is a scoop, not sharp, and this is its form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the blade cutting towards the buttock at the core, and the scoop blade towards the bone, and keep it in place until it reaches the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And scrape all the vessels that descend along the eyes until the incision is continuous up to those that open at the core, and then make another cut in the middle cut up to the other side; and then extract the blood evenly, and press out the lymph for the blood taken; then place a tent of old cotton in each cut, and cover with moist cloths in wine and oil and grease, and guard that abscesses do not appear; and on the third day untie the bandage, and apply a large dressing of warm water, then cure with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of eye pain
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone frequently gets acute catarrh, and you see the eyes swollen and small, with weakening of vision, and burning paper; and the nose secretes a watery discharge, and causes pain; and the patient sneezes; then know from these symptoms that these materials and this catarrh come only from many veins, and the treatment that is effective is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you should instruct the patient to look behind their forehead, then make a large incision through the forehead, and another one of lesser width.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And start from the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision go until the bone is exposed; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating. When the bone is uncovered, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then separate between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton and linen; then cover above with moistened cloth in wine and oil, and guard against hot abscesses; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with excitative things that cause flesh to grow.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In a manner: take two parts of flour of wheat, and four parts of colocynth, and make a poultice; and apply it to the wounds to draw out flesh throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stopping up of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into ears is one of four things: or grains, or beast, or mineral stone or similar thing such as iron; or seed, such as oats, beans, peas; or effluents such as water and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear a stone or some other kind of thing that does not stick to the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if it distils a little violet oil or safflower oil, then proceed with its extraction; and cause him to sneeze by condisi, and plug his nostrils when he sneezes, and put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and keep the ear above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often it comes to discharge through this treatment; and if it does not come to discharge, proceed with the extraction using fine forceps, of which the form is described here.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it discharges through the forceps, that is good; if not, proceed with the extraction using a fine awl of small thickness; and if it does not discharge through this, make an araignée cane and insert the head of the cane or hole of the ear firmly, and plug the area around the cane with soft wax so that the liquid cannot enter with the cane; then draw it out thoroughly, for often it discharges as we have said; and if it does not discharge in this manner, take glue and place the tweezers in it, and put any instrument that is suitable for this into place, and put a bit of cotton inside; then press the glue over the stone or whatever it is, and draw it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not break from all these things that we have said, hasten to incise the ear as one would an abscess, and spasm; and the manner of incision is that you first draw the patient into a position favorable for the operation, and extract the blood according to the measure of its virtue, then place the patient's ear between your hands and turn it upward, and make a small incision at the root of the ear where the fat or bone depends; and let the incision be as narrow as a crescent until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your power, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is enclosed and swollen, administer the extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the spatule with a thin blade according to this form.
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think the grains are moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine tongs and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction be easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the water that falls into the ear, then the patient should use nose blowing with initial conditions, and plug the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them lie on that same ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it drains forcefully through that, that is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not, take many stones according to the length of your fingers and make them warm on fire. And place one stone in the patient's ear and hold another piece of stone from the other side, striking the stone in the ear with a different stone. Do not stop striking stone against stone until the water drains forcefully out, and thus it will drain forcefully. If you see this, take a rush, and insert one end of the rush into the ear, and the other end near fire until the softer part of the rush is burned. Then repeat with other rushes until the water drains completely, as we have said in the case of stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, like a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size and can be felt, use forceps for the extraction; and this is the thing easiest to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure them as we have said in the division and treat distillations, and if the cure does not help much, then you must look at the ear in the sunlight: if there are visible worms, remove them with fine forceps, and if they do not appear, take the wick of cotton mentioned here.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is narrow inside and wide outside.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the most subtle thread into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then thoroughly along the canal; do this often until all the wax comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, stuff the ear canal with cotton as I have said for stones; and if they do not protrude forcefully as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in the extraction of worms, and you will find them treated in the section on distillations; and distill your oils and medicines into the ear with this instrument, of which the form is as you see.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be made of thin silver or tin wire with small holes on the sides and above for distillation; and to press within the distillation apparatus, use a well-made iron instrument for this purpose. If you wish, take a razor and wrap a fitting piece of cotton around its point; then pour in your oil or juice, and the medicines you desire into the canal, with the canal in the ear. Then insert the razor fully into the cotton, and press firmly with your hand until the oil is distilled or movement from the ear ceases. Let the mixture cool slightly over fire as when distilling into the ear; and ensure it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the blocking of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who has no perforation in the ears; and the same thing happens to adults due to a wound blocking up or a tumor growing inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes come so completely that one cannot see them; and sometimes the perforation is just barely blocked, and the opening can still be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes so completely blocked that one cannot see it is of great concern for treatment, and in such cases, you must place the ear of the patient in the sun; and look inside: if you see the visible blockage or opilation, then the work has been completed.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not damage the ear; if the excision is of new flesh or an ear wax mass, hold it with fine forceps, and remove it gently, until all the flesh is taken out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the excision is performed in the ear, take the fine razor gently and heat it a little on fire, then place it over the ear wax.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the excision causes pain in the ear, pierce it gently, and make sure not to damage the nerves of the ear; then place a wick in the ear according to the size of the opening, and smear it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this on any day while the wound is healing, or take a tent and marrow in rose water, and powder on glass vitriol ground; and if you see swollen ear, it must be that you remove the tent and apply another moistened tent made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is removed; then treat until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, soak a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments that remove the bleeding which are or involve distillation.
de la char des papieres	from the juice of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that comes from papers of eyes when they are moist and are dried, you must extend them with tongs and forceps, and cover the head with a spatule made from its roots; then place on the head glass vitriol ground.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without scraping, cauterize with the delicate lens cautery, and the cauterizer after incision moves; often they return, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return at all.
de la gresle	Of the hailstone.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often come from the eyes things that resemble hailstones in their shape and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "hail," and it is a collection of moisture large on the surface and underneath; the procedures are such: observe whether the hail moves from one side to another, and this is a light matter to know; then make it wide, then burn each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and extract it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cope it without piercing a little the paper, it does not harm the patient at all; and if the wound is large,缝合并用线缝合，直到它痊愈；如果很小，则无需用力，因为膏药很快就能治愈并促进肉芽组织生长。
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the gravel descends into the inner ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and remove the gravel with tweezers, and cope and press it from one side to the other; and if the paper is removed by incision, it does not harm anything; and when the gravel is coped, wash the eye with salt water, and cure the head of what promotes flesh growth until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is embedded in the membranes of paper-like structures above, and this happens more to children than to adults, and greatly grieves their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and for this reason, they lie down on their faces and sleep there, and are covered with their damp paper-like membranes that inflame and obscure the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the shoulder between your fingers and feel the exinach within.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head on your lap; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity contained by the exinach from each part, then place it over him; and press with your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered within the circle; then make a groove in the middle of the moist area, cutting a slit wide enough, and not more than the wound made in the healthy vein; and let the skin grow perfectly until you see the exinach; and from many dispositions, the exinach comes out through the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the wound completely and place a piece of cloth between your fingers at the edge. Turn your hand to the right and to the left until it is spread; and keep watch that you do not injure the fender, that you do not come all the way to the spatumile up to the eye, that you do not blind him.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the extract does not open at the beginning of the fender, widen the opening slightly until it opens; then extract as we have said, then apply moistened cloth and water, and place over the edge, and extract with threads.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if such men who grind grain and put it there to腐化 those remaining moistures.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat until he is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is an abscess hot in the wound, treat with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When on paper hairs grow other than those natural, and they are mature, they harm the eyes, and bring about conditions similar to habituated tearing and softening of the paper and albugine, such that it is a cause for the destruction of the eyes; and the treatment is according to four methods: either by applying fire cauterization together with heat, or by medicinal treatments as described in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by cairnes [a type of cauterizing tool], according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the head of the patient in your healthy hand, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it is turned inward, that is good; if not, insert a needle along the thread above; let this be from the margin of the paper or where the hair grows among these hairs, and draw the thread upwards over the entire paper, then cut it off with the razor; then make an incision under the paper, beneath the added hairs, to all the spatumile copant, from the large tearer to the small one; then extract the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and silk under the paper, then sign over the paper a figure of enchye, as the laurel leaf, and always it must be that the figure is according to the quantity that you wish to lift from the paper which is divided for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if one needs much of the paper according to how it is softened; then make at all the spatumile above the two lines that you have signed, and start from the large lacrimal jusc’a small; and let there be one of the cracks near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put an ounce in one of the II angles of the keur, then burn it completely; then join the II lips with a stitch using a needle and all the fine wool thread, and wipe away the blood, and do away with the superfluous threads above the II sorcilz at any sticky things, if you wish to make this; and if not, have no care for it, then leave the stitch and the threads until III days or IV; then cure the wound without a stitch using dry and constraining things, because the paper revives suddenly from the wound and its joining, but the stitch is worn out (as the ancients said), and these are works without fear; and in another manner: and it is that you mark the paper with a figure which is as like the leaf of laurel, as we have recounted, at III ounces severed according to the form which is here.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply those that surpass the small forces evenly according to the form which is given here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the things are not equal, take a needle or thread, and put one thread through the figure; and place the other thread beside the large wound, and the second thread beside the small one, and assemble between your two hands the threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above what you have marked, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes from your incision, soothe it with cerate and similar soothing ointment; and any time the hair of the paper is reversed, you must use what we said about the incision; but the stitching on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the canes is according to this form: and it is that you convert the paper and the fen[de] within according to what I have said, and then make two canes by art, and two fine threads as long as the paper and as wide as the space between the fingers; and cope with the two heads of the parts where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly above that which rises from the paper of the eye, and restrain the two canes from the two sides form[ed]; and let it thus for some days, and the skin which was restrained will die and nerve and perish, until it falls by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, then cope with strength, and cure until it is sane. And when the wound is healed, and the paper is lifted, and no hairs will grow; and this is the form of the two canes that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The operations are such that you insert a fine needle, and thread a thin silk thread through it; then join the heads and tie them tightly together, and let the lengths of the threads be one palm long; then sew another thin silk thread briefly, and tie its head to the thread; then put the patient's head into your healthy side; and keep away from the sun so that the operations may become clear, for it is a fine and delicate work. Then insert the needle along the root of the added hair, and make it pierce through the hastern paper quickly as you pull it over the natural hair; then extract the hair up to the seam in the paper, and put into the seam that hair if there be one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that all the hairs emerge from the seam with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not grow out with it, you shall draw the chase away from above to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase seems to have passed through the perforation and that you see it by the eye's vision; then you shall draw the chase and the thread, close the wound and let it close for two or three days, until the hairs grow in their place and flesh grows above; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair of natural hair, and raise it with that or leave it, until it is elongated and then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the putrefaction of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the putrefaction, comes into the oil, there are two ways of it: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or surgery, or the fire cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of the work in it is that you cut the suture, and separate the edges of it, and put linen tents inside, and tie it until it is healed; and it is not fitting that you use in the treatment of it things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the illness returns worse than the first; but use works of softening things, such as fenugreek; and washes with water or urine and linseed that is cooked, and ointments melted into any of the oils, and wrap it in a tent, and treat it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care so that it does not heal entirely according to the form it was before; and these works that we have said are only remedies for this disease, so that it does not return according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the flesh that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accidental comes from wounds and splits and cauteries and similar things; and the way of this work is that you take a needle, in which there be double thread, and fix it in the flesh, and make the thread pierce from left lachrymal gland to right, so that the threads come out at both heads of the flesh; then leave the flesh above on all sides by the needle, and the cloth on the broad sponge.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the crack, turn the paper, and make two cracks inside the paper; and let the heads of the two cracks be at the angles of the incision you have made, and make such angles that when they are assembled, the figure is as one would be for a letter which has no "i griseche"; then remove the flesh according to the quantity that its edges are cut from underneath, from what follows the paper, then attach the two separated parts with a linen thread; then apply the cure of what we have said about softening medicines and tents until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a crack or suture or cautery, you must make a full crack underneath the hairs of the paper, according to what is said before; then separate between the two flaps of a tent as I have said; and one must perform the work according to the form of the disease, for it is much diverse in form. The master surgeons prepare devices with all their skill so that they may make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what needs to be done and instruments in various preparations.
dou soudement de la papiere	suddenly from the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this缝合 happens to a person in such a manner that the paper above is hardened with the white of an egg, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must accordingly put the point of a needle under the paper, and lift it up; and hold it with forceps until you cut away what is attached to the fine spatumile, which should not be too harsh or too sharp so that the patient cannot endure the spatumile being too harsh or bleaching the eye; and make your incision, by which you burn together the assembled parts gently, so that the paper returns according to its natural form; and all that is assembled heals completely, and does not create any once in an aigui salee eye, and lifts with sweet water, and from anger; then place between the paper and the eye a tent of linen, and put on the eye wet wool soaked in abundant egg; and after three days use binding things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The nail of the eye is according to two manners: it is nervous and seems like a hard cornea, and another which is not nervous but seems like white moist ice, that when touched with iron and carefully tended with tweezers, one cannot remove; and both seem to begin near the large lacrimal gland, growing little by little until they cover all vision and all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the patient place their head on your lap, then open their eyes; and lift the paper with your hand, then clip the nail with small tweezers, stretching it above; then take a needle, and put horse hair, or goat hair, or beef hair, and a strong thread. Double the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing through the entire length of the needle, and attach the nail to a thread, stretching it above, and scrape along the side of the nail that leaves the seam and the silk up to the root, then cut off the remaining part from the lacrimal gland to the fine spatumile with small force, leaving the natural skin or lacrimal gland, so that the body does not produce tears through this incision as it is accustomed; sometimes only the nail and thread are stretched, as we have said; then scrape along all the fine spatumile where its form lies.
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And beware that the spatule does not touch the fleshy lining and does not tear it, and that the probe is not perforated; and after the incision, pour a little sieved salt into the eye, and a collar made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then treat with what is needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot pierce it with the needle, and the awls cannot enter, often this resemblance of a nail is treated with medicines; and they come to pass as I have recounted in the division, and if you see it copulate, work on the eye of the patient, and take the spatule slightly sharp according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And scrape the nail gently from above, and if you see that it thins slightly and the root presses closer, distill into the eye from your mouth a collar made of litharge and a red collar and sieved salt, and plug the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same method until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, such as an abscess, then let it alone, and first treat the warm abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the gland causes great harm to the eye, suspend it by an oncine, and excise a part but not entirely, so that tears do not arise; then distill into the eye red powder made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises around the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Of some men's eyes, red flesh arises once and covers the pupil, is fixed on paper and turned to drain, seeming like a hyacinth flower; and the work is such that the patient places his head in your good direction, then turns the eyes, and all this red flesh is removed with appropriate oncines, and it is suspended by force; then excise the first flesh, and continue cutting close until the end, and take care not to injure the eye during the work; and let the incision of the ciliary body be as we have said in the incision of the nail with small forces from which one removes the swelling, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is completed and all flesh is removed, fill the eye with ground salt or distill red powder into it and use wet cloth with egg yolk over the eye to ensure a warm abscess; if nothing remains and the wound heals well, and you are unsure of a warm abscess, leave the eye and treat the abscess with things that soothe a warm abscess; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do for any further flesh that arises in the eye by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But nevertheless, it must be that you adjust the treatment of each weak eye from the natural way; and from the accidental way, in the work of iron; and not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this limb suffers from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	If the veins around the eyes are red and cover the eye, they allow the work to be seen and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, it is necessary for the first step that you examine whether the eye, where the redness is, is out, and there is no other disease besides the redness; then proceed in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your healthy hand, then suspend those veins by an ounce according to your wisdom, and let the ounces be doubly subtle according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be two ounces by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then coil the veins subtly with forceps, and wipe away the blood hour after hour until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to damage the eye with the points of the forceps, and perform this work at midday in front of the sun, and be very hot in your work so that you do not harm any veins; and when you have done this, distill in the eye a mixture of green and red colcothar to corrupt what remains of the swelling.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot coil all of them in that hour, apply a poultice to the eye with things that soothe the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pains are soothed and assured that the hot abscess is gone, then resume this method as described until it is healed; and this is the form of the forceps.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula of the eye
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire (fistula) is called "arissati": when you cure it with cautery and medicine of hot water as I have said before, and it is not healed, then you indeed cut over the abscess, in the place where it should die, and draw out all the moisture that is in it, until the bone is revealed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is revealed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then proceed with all the instrument of which this is the form; and it is called "asperchief," and be made from iron to the head of it, and be pointed like a rasp as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the bone patch of the corrupted one, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little so that you know that the corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the bone patch of medicinal desiccatives.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is fused, and flesh arises, and the core of the bone is fused, and remains thus for 40 days, and it does not regenerate and is not an abscess, and no bad accident occurs, know that it is healed; if not, there is another way to bring the fistula back to the perforation of the neck according to this form: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron and with wet medicines, and when it is uncovered, take a saw according to this form, and let the iron head have three angles, and the shaft be thin until the tip as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then place it on the bone near the eye, and keep your hand away from the eye a little, then turn to all the forest until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it by the fluid that is there if he keeps his hand on his nose; and then restore the head of medicine with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the head, the matter goes to the nose; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the discharge of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are completely opened, and there is no dislocation or reduction, it is necessary to tie the patient. Then heal them, then place cups or pustules without piercing to suck, then put on the eye a lien made of myrrh and aloes and incense and sarcolle, and then drain the eye, and plaster with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft enough cloths, double each one four times, and then place one over the other according to the quantity the eyes need. Then drain it from above with a hard form bandage, and repeat the cups to suck without piercing; then remove the cups and let the eye be held day and night, and if the lien becomes soft, you must tighten it much; then remove the lien after day and night, and if you see the eye heal, that is good; but if not, continue with the plastering and cloths and lien and cups until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	for the tearing of a vein
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	when disruptions come in the vein, then open and burst, coming out like grains of resin, and are shocking to see; then if you see it coped, the operations are such that you stick a needle at the root of the part beneath until above, then stick another needle with double thread from the eyelid part; and make it pierce, and let the first needle remain according to its position; then cut the leu of the double thread and tie a part of the vein around, and hold it tightly, then remove the needle and put on the eye a cloth moistened in abundance of egg; and leave it until the threads are healed with the vein, then cure the eye with things that comfort as long as the wound is sound; and at no time restrain the wound from every part of a circle of cloth until it is sound.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes show great appearance, pierce them with a sharp needle coming from the temple next to the eye, drain the white moisture and let the eyes drop in quickly; then extract them when they are healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the socket of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not in the socket of the eye which is gathered in the eye, seeming like water descending, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you cause the patient to sit on a chair properly aligned, then take the head between your hands from one side, and move the neck until you see the socket come above your eyes; then pierce it, and do not let it descend, and clear the light, and the patient will see things as they should; and if it does not descend underneath, know that it is water, and if the descents of the socket are not aligned as we have said, know that it is water.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you seat the patient between your hands, then take the fine spatula and make incisions on the corneal membrane gradually along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane and the corona, until the bow is out; and when it has emerged, distill hot aqueous honey or boiled fenugreek water mixed with honey into the eye, then cure it with another dressing until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye's waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have placed the similarities of the eye's waters in the division, and those that need to be pierced; work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you seat the patient between your hands crossed, away from sunlight, and tie the healthy eye tightly; then place the paper of the eye on your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or on your right hand if they are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument called "almagda," or on your left hand, if the eyes are right-handed; then put the point of the instrument near the corona by the thickness of a finger into that part of the outer canthus where the tear duct is located, and firmly insert the instrument called "almagda" so that it pierces through the inner corner of the eye, feeling when almagda reaches the empty space; and the size of the path of almagda should be precisely equal to the measure from the prunele to the end of the noirour; this is the corona of the eye; you will see the bone in that paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then place the instrument directly where the fluid is, and express it through another passage.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the liquid flows out now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the liquid rises again by the second vein, apply force with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place and no longer rises, gently extract it by turning your hand slowly; then put a bit of silk thread around it, and remove this from the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place something to plug the eye, such as a moistened piece of wool in rose oil and abundant egg, and secure it with healthy eye tissue.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those of our time, we place on with a cloth soaked in abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if it hardens to the extent that it cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are people whose eyes are too hard, then you must use the instrument called "alberit", of which its form is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce then the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then pour in the hardening substance as we have said; and at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient a sleeping position in the dark place on his back; and let him be free from all movements, and give him light foods, and move neither his head nor to the right nor to the left, and bind him according to his condition until three days; then release him in that same dark room, and test his vision, and have him show some things, and then rebind him until seven days; and it is not fitting that you do this during the time of treatment or after incision now, but you must loosen it, because the fluid rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess is present, you release the eye before the seventh day, and follow the treatment for one who alleviates an abscess; when it is pacified, you release the vision and place over its face a small skin to cover any day, and let it be in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then leave the house little by little, and adapt to it; know that no deacon should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And some twenty came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in their country they made almagda puncts, which they suck with water, but truly I never saw any such thing in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of scabies, for he who does not know them will be deceived; and they are properly of arsenic.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of aus be of this same subtlety, and the last in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh near the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there arise or appear malformed noses, of which some seem to have the feet of scorpions; and there are such that have a nose embedded in flesh of a dark color, and others with a nose sprouting from flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	For those noses that are sprouting but not embedded, you must place the patient between your hands against the sun; work on his nostrils, and sprinkle an ounce of powder over those noses, and remove them. Proceed carefully with what you can sustain at the subtle acute point from one side, until you know that the nose is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any thing that we cannot cope with, open it completely with all the subtle instruments gently, so that nothing remains; and if it surmounts without or an abscess chaus, give him the help as it should be; and if it is malign abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the pus be stanched and all the flesh be removed, then throw out ash, oil, or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the nose heals and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that there is new flesh grown on the bone above, where the instruments could not reach: then you must put a slightly thick linen thread, which has been knotted by our hands, between each knot with enough or less space; and place the patient's head at the nostril end in such a way as to allow the thread to be drawn through the nostril into the mouth; and many times children do this at school, and it is a light thing for him who knows how to do it; then hold the chief that comes through the nostril with one hand, and the other chief that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and draw them alternately while attending to us who are with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it so that you know the nerves have corrupted that flesh, then draw the thread, wipe the blood, soften the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back in place as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all that remains of the flesh; then put a cane of plonc in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if it needs drying medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, to which one distills the eyes and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be made of silver or lead, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it in thus; and if you see, make it a closed cane, and let the instrument be full for purging the head; have one hand at the head to hold it when we heat the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	many times a disease arises at the top of the nose called "telul", grows and becomes large, to such an extent that it is visible upon looking; and because of this, you must lance it at the beginning, and extract all the pus, then apply a fire cautery or burning medicine over it; and if one delays lancing until it becomes large, one must be careful if it is hard, of a fleshy color, and has little sense: do not touch it with iron at all because it is an embedded abscess, for when it is lanced once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is due to heat contact, not of a fleshy color, and you can see that one can lance it completely, empty the patient and lance carefully without fear, and cure it with dry and constricting things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	When solutions of continuation come to one of these cartilages in the work, it profits little, for in some men.
