Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to any person, examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; then approximate the two lips with a缝合，直到痊愈；如果嘴唇一侧干燥而另一侧湿润，那么必须将所有部分的边缘灼烧直至痊愈，然后用一线缝合，并绷紧，撒上龙血石粉末，研碎的香料；再在粉末上放置一块强力膏药或其他粘贴膏药，直到自行愈合，之后涂抹油膏直至痊愈。
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of stitching is such that you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in suturing the belly; or by thread, as I have made known to you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses of lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	By hand, abscesses appear in the lips hard, resembling grains of wheat, small and large; then it must be that you turn the lips, incise on each side, and take out each part with forceps; then apply leu after the incision of vitriole broiet, until the blood is stanched; and then apply linseed, and cure the leu with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a hard bump arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; it must be held with tongs and cut at its root, allowing the juice or blood to flow; then place vitriol powder or other drying powders over the head; if that bump returns after incision, often it happens, so cut again and cauterize: it does not return after the cauterization; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of sorts
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, bumps are assembled at the root of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scaly skin that is ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellowish and worm-eaten, as decay comes to the gums, making the teeth stinky; it must be that you place the patient in your hands, and their head on your lap, and remove any teeth or scales visible, until nothing remains; thus clean the blackness and greenishness and yellowness and other stains, until they are all removed; and if what is to be removed according to the first reason is good, it is well; but if not, you must start again on the second day and the third, until you have cleaned everything; know that teeth need various forms of instruments to clean them, depending on which type of work they show, because the rasps used to remove teeth have different shapes from those used between the teeth; these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat the tooth for its pain, you should delay the extraction as long as possible, for it must not be done at all if one can help it; for it is a substance very high up so that one cannot have any excuse for removing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is constrained to extraction, it must be certain which tooth aches.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain deceives the patient, and they think it is from a sound tooth, and have the good tooth extracted; but in any case, the pain does not depart because of this until the bad tooth is removed, for we have often done so to these patients. And when you are well certain which tooth aches, it must be that you scrape around the tooth with a sharp instrument to protect the gum on all sides; then move it gently or with fine forceps at first little by little, until it is thoroughly loosened, then firmly secure the forceps; and place the patient's head in your lap between your knees, and hold them well so they do not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After drawing the tooth rightly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, take any of these instruments and insert it gently from each side, and move it as you have done before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten into, it must be filled with wadding, lint, or cotton; and you should grip it gently with forceps so that it does not break when gripping; and you must work carefully around the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care that you do not break it and leave a part behind, as this will cause the patient greater pain than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care that you do not do it as the ignorant surgeon does, who, through their haste and boldness, break the root once and do not provide what we have described; but they bring about great illness one time by incision due to the roots remaining or because of the bone they broke, as we often see. And when the tooth is drawn, wash the mouth with wine or oil of olive and salt; and if there is bleeding, which often occurs, fill the mouth with vitriol powder; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one must first pull the teeth, should be long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have thick handles so that they do not bend when extracting, and let them be made of well-forged iron, and let them have teeth to hold tightly.
de la racine des dens	from the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary to place moistened cotton with butter on the wound for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is healed, then use the forceps called "algefri," of which the head resembles a surgical tool; and let them be made similarly to a file, and that is their shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to come out with all these tongs, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh completely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be firm and large so that it does not break easily, and if the root breaks through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you need to use an instrument that has two prongs, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are in front according to the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument that seems like large tongs, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let it be that this instrument cannot be broken, and know that few dental instruments are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the master surgeons find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their work and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the old ones did not teach any instrument because of the diversity of teeth, or if they break a part of the bone or another bone, or it rots, then one seeks the instruments that it is necessary to have, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well-holding to keep the bone from escaping, but able to hold and remove it; then restore its place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, then let it be treated with all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to the natural course, and their form is ugly, especially in maiden women, you must know whether the teeth are born after the gum, and are not in the right place, and cannot be soothed nor smoothed: then you should file them; and if they are misaligned with the gum, take this instrument whose shape is as that of a small beak, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And file the teeth little by little in your hand for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that they can be smoothed, then smooth them with a piece of fine sandpaper as described.
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the sandpaper used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little in your hand over several days gently, so that it does not move while it heals; then level it off at the end with a rasp. If the tooth is too sharp and causes the tongue to turn white, you must smooth its sharpness until it is equal, so that it does not turn the tongue white nor corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth chatter
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the front teeth chatter due to percussion or falling, and the patient cannot press against what he eats without defecating, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, it is not effective; so you must restrain them with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes. And let the threads be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to align the teeth, take the thread and bend it double between two healthy teeth, then place the points between the adjacent teeth, whether one or more, until you see clearly to the healthy tooth on the other side; then re-cover from where you began, and extract your hand delicately and carefully, so that it does not move at all; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the shoulder with a needle using forceps, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it such that it does not damage the tongue; and then leave it so tight as it can remain, and if it loosens or the threads break, restrain it with another thread; if it remains and serves thus for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the alignment of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, frequently as we have said; and one must not do so except by those who are skilled and suffer, and once the form of an osseous tooth of a deer is made, one places it in the place where it is missing, and restrains it as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover up the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	no wound from the tongue by nature or accident comes thus; or by an accidental injury to a缝合的伤口；手术过程是这样的，你张开病人的嘴巴，让他的头靠在你的肩上，然后松开舌头；随后覆盖住大的神经伤口，直到舌头脱离其位置为止；如果有硬块或血肿，并且是由创伤突然引起的，那么使用钩针并从大血管下方的空隙中剪断该连接；注意不要让切口过于完美，以免损伤下面的大动脉；做完后，用玫瑰水或茴香水，或者冷水冲洗伤口，然后在舌头上放一块亚麻布绷带；每晚让病人躺下，确保伤口不会感染。
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding continues, put on the shoulder powdered glass; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a boil that is of a red, black, or hard color, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is turning white and there is moisture, you should lance it with an oncine weight, and make a small incision with a sharp lancet, and drain it on both sides; and if the blood does not stop during your treatment, put powdered glass on it until it is healed, then return to your treatment as long as you need to; afterwards remove the dressing of silk and salt, and treat with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are lumps in the throat called "godath," and these are properly known as two almonds. When you cure them, as we have said in the division, and if they are hard abscesses with small size and flesh-colored, be careful not to touch them with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, do not touch them with iron at all, also for the evacuation of blood; but leave them until they are ripe, and then you can cut them, or they would break on their own. And if they are white in color and the root is fine, prepare the instrument to extract them, but first see if the abscess has cooled down and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, seat the patient facing the sun, and his head in your care, and let him close his mouth, and the sergeant hold the tool between his hands, pressing the tongue underneath the entire instrument, which is its form; it should be made of silver or fine tin as thin as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	You press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, take an ounce and the prong in the almond shape, and draw force more on top than you can; then do not pull anything from the tissues, just withdraw it, which is its form, seeming like strong forces; and both ends are curved and one against the other, and are very sharp, made of iron indurated or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, use tongs, of which the form is:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and blunt on the other; and when you have incised one of the almonds, incise the other in the same manner. After the incision, gargle the patient with hot, sharp water, or with sharp water and easy to swallow. If bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with cold water, or cooked pomegranate peel, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stanched. Then cure the wound when it is healed; and if other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two almonds, incise them in the same manner as the two almonds evenly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that had grown within her throat, namely the small abscess; and had almost completely closed the throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the obstructed passage, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she had remained like that for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had to be lanced through both openings of the neck.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then soon, and inserted the lancet into one opening, then drew out a large portion of the pus; then I reinserted it into the other opening of the neck, and cleaned her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the lancet into these abscesses, and drained part of it, and only a little bit of blood came out; and thus the passage in her throat was unclosed, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued cutting at this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept recurring and filled up the space that I had drained until it became very large; then I treated it and cauterized inside her throat: thus it stopped from growing further; and I left those matters, and only let God decide what would happen to her after me.
de l’uve	from the eye socket
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When swelling occurs in the eye socket and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and when it is large and round, it is called "uve.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are calmed and are fine, then it is appropriate to lance it; and that which is round gathered and is not long; and which is bloody or of linen color or black, then it is appropriate to avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it in the manner as I have said, instruct the patient to sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned earlier; then insert the oncine into the eye socket, draw it out, and lance it using the two instruments as described in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut more than the superfluous that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it grieves to the voice and speech; and after incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of cutting, you must use an instrument for the cautery to alleviate their fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patient put their head on your side, and then press their tongue with the instrument we mentioned or cautery chapter, and cover it with live water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and fill the mouth of this instrument as shown here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a head or where one puts the medicine, as the hairs of a spoon, and place the instrument above the eye with all the medicine; and let the patient lie on his side, so that saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not descend to the throat and the blepharitis; then hold your hand above the medicine and press it against the eye, for half an hour in quantity, until you see nerves and the bites of the medicine are pacified; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the instrument under the cotton on top of the conjunctiva; and do this often until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five days. And if you need to re-start the cautery with the medicine, do so, and after the cautery wash it around the eye with cotton stuffed in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be rinsed with cold water, and cured with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take calamus and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and avens and similar herbs, and gather all of them or some of them in a pot, and place them easily, and cause them to boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and within the pot have the instrument covered according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And may be of silver or tin, and may one of the heads be inserted in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the cane, until the eye is numbed; after which renew often, until the eye dries up, and ensure that you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things may occur; and do not do this when the abscess is declining.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an eggshell inside the chimney for the patient so that it is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to weigh down on the mouth, and this is a good treatment overall for health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it is necessary to remove bone or spiny fish flesh or any other thing. Therefore, you should treat what you can see and press the tongue under the instrument towards the sun so that you see the thing move. For what does not appear and lies in the throat, you should make the patient vomit as if the meat were cooked in the stomach; by chance, it may be expelled by vomiting; or the patient might swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread. Tie the sponge with a thread and then swallow it. When it comes to the place, it will be removed, and you can then extract it. If it does not come out as described above, take the plonging instrument in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the forceps be applied to the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and keep the head lifted high; and see that you do not touch the epiglottis, lest you hurt it or push the bone in; and move such that the patient exhales, for then he will breathe easier; if he breathes out, or if air is forced to all parts of the instrument equally, as long as it is forced.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood from the throat is treated with medicine as I have said in the division through the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient in the sunlight, after you press his tongue with the instrument I have mentioned.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the pus, draw it out with a very small lancet, or with fine forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, take a live cane, insert it into the throat of the patient, then blow or shake the cane with hot air, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient is thirsty all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full glass of cold water, pour it into the mouth, and give it to swallow, and move it with his hand often; and as soon as the pus detects the water, let it fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with arsenic sulfide, using the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the uvea; do this many times, for it will fall without difficulty.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are glowing coals, and let it be covered with a perforated cover on top, and through that perforation place the head of the instrument; then throw the fumigation into it, and the patient put the end of the cane in their mouth, and close the mouth, so that the smoke does not escape but goes to the flesh; and the blood will now fall out. And if it does not fall, you must repeat the fumigation many times; and allow the patient to be thirsty, and eat salty and dry things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out through this regimen.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument with which one treats the blood, is such that when one can see it, it resembles bent tongs to enter into the throat; and it has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has a roughness like sandpaper, so that whatever it takes, it cannot release; and behold its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many similitudes of abscesses are, according to what the memory brings hereafter in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and there are two ways of which one is in its very similitude, and of that which it retains moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the sores or where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are different from those of the solid part, and abscesses of flesh are different from those that come in joints, and each has its judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And for abscesses, one must not pierce them until the bowels are dead according to their completion; and there are some that require piercing when they are ripe, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from joints, and one lets them remain until they are rotten within, by chance the ligaments and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or when the abscess is from the principal limb, and if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; or when it is from the foundation, one should pierce it in the same way once it is dead; and it does not matter that you perforate an abscess that has not yet completed digestion, except for that which is from the foundation, so that it does not rot completely and become a fistula; and it cannot heal over a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of perforating the abscess that is dead according to completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the reduction in pain and redness, and the swelling and sharpness at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should place the perforation where more dependent upon the abscess, and where it appears to move. Let the perforation be as long as the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere else equally without any folds.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the living flesh, it is better to let the perforation remain until digestion is completed, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you perforate before that, the body will be lengthened by the venom of it, and it is full of much filth; and perchance the edges and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is perforated according to the size of the body, as the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it must be that you administer small punctures for small abscesses and large punctures for large abscesses, and many slits according to the size of the abscess. And for such abscesses where it is necessary to make a keyhole, cover; when it has become as hard as a grape stone and is softened, you must do so as with buboes: and for those that are slit in three angles, and for those from which one covers like the leaf of laurel, as with angry abscesses; and for those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, as with a superficial abscess, it must be pierced completely; and when the abscess is large, and has formed a significant boil, if you pierce it, do not draw out all of the pus in that hour, but only part of it; then seal the abscess until the next day, and draw out some more; do this many times gradually, until all the pus exits; similarly, if the patient has weak virtue, or is a pregnant woman, or small children, or elderly and decrepit individuals.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Because the patient trembles several times with the discharge of the pus, that by chance kills the patient, and you will not know this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and look to see if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a complete incision, apply pieces of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there are many openings, it must be that you insert a tent into each so they come against one another; and if you have cut through the skin in the abscess and sewed it up, it must be filled with old cotton or lint soaked in linseed oil, and tied for three days; then remove it, and treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is an evacuation of blood in your work, you apply cold water and ease the pain, and cover with soft linen, and place over the area where the blood flows repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the evacuation of blood persists, you apply treatment and care, and the powders that I have said to be used in this book, whether it is winter and the limbs or abscesses are particularly nervous, then it is necessary for you to place over tents and soft linens soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is summer, and the limbs are fleshy, then it is necessary for you to place soft linens soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, up to the third day, as we have said; and then remove the abscess, dry it, and treat it as needed until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	of the sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or come from the head small abscesses, and they are like those in fabrics, as with the fibers of a flax plant, and there are many that resemble them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and like those with moisture, similar to pulses; and there are some that are hard and stony to the touch, and there is no doubt if the artery does not cause contrary effects.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operations of the flank are such that you test with any instrument called "intromissory," from which the form follows, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, he lets it drain from above downward.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, he cauterizes without leaving any skin on the part containing that moisture, because it repeatedly dislocates if nothing is left; then he dips cotton in Egyptian ointment if present; otherwise, in water and salt, and applies it to the wound, letting it remain until the next day; and this allows what has remained from the night to drain.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then he resumes applying the cotton, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that nothing remains from the night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds much fat, shape the incision according to this form, long; and cut with all your strength, and burn it from all sides, and put all your effort into drawing out the pus where it lies; and if the artery acts against you, do as I have said after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is stony, and cut and treat as I have said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut for the stony abscess and its moisture is lighter, because they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if some of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and these were the abscesses that I cut from an old woman; and found the abscess as a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if any had been made from it, one would have also made a wound from it like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head or cheeks, these that come from the roots of the ears, the incision should be all day at the most dependent part of the body, to allow the boil to escape; and the treatment as it should.
des scrophules	of gland swellings
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times such abscesses occur in the neck, under the armpits, and in angles, and sometimes appear elsewhere on the body, they are hard, and are joined together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each gland swelling is properly within its own cavity, like the lump and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities in these gland swellings.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are those that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see in good disposition by touch, and resemble the color of the body, and move from every part and are not raw on the neck nor near the artery nor the conduit, and are not deep; it is fitting that you cauterize from above, and scorch each part, and draw the two lips of the heart with needles if you need to, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw a little bit by little bit, and be sure that you do not cauterize the nerve nor the vein, and let neither spatumile, agus, nor trenching occur, so that your hand does not slip, and does not go too far, so that you do not cauterize what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you puncture the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to operate, put vitriol powder or any other substances that staunch blood in the wound, and bind the wound; and leave it until the abscess is pacified, and the wound becomes softened, and begins to腐烂。
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the abscess is staunched, return to your work until you complete it; then rest according to your proper indication if there remain any small scrofulous swellings, and drain and cleanse them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofulous swelling, it is not suitable to puncture that swelling at its root. Instead, ligate it with a double strong thread, and let it fall away through it without harm. Then dress the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and treat it further.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound, and suture them now, since there is no longer any excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you cut the root of it, and draw out the force, and suture it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce it where it apertures most; and pierce it thus as the one previously said, hanging down, then apply wicks with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, continue the ointment treatment until it is healed.
de squinance	of scrophula
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of the surgery of the throat; but I have never seen anyone perform it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have scrophula, it is necessary to cut the incision in the throat which is called "epiglote"; and if no help is sought from this, because all the veins and the tumour of the sick are hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the tonsil, it is necessary to cut the epiglote to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It must therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglote, be cut over three or four small slits from side to side, between the two circles or according to the size of the slit made thereby; not in the cartilage; and those who are so treated are suitable for the cutting of the epiglote as there is no flesh, and the vessels are long within.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it must be stretched from the throat to the entire inch, then cut the skin until it comes to the vein; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see anything, and then scrape the flesh as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the flow of the vein which leaps forth through the broken part, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound in the heart, and suture it thoroughly beneath the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce flesh until he is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis said that this should not be done until the throat is completely numb, and the patient is judged to be dying, and then proceed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then lift the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and for this, the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease passes, and it passes in three or four days. Then they commanded to stitch and treat the wound until it is healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I see that a damsela took the knife, and pierced her throat, and cut part of the cord from the heart; and I was called to perform the cure, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood issuing from it. I knew that she had not pierced a vein nor any great artery, but the blood was coming from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, sewed the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and the damsela did not suffer from hoarseness, and returned to her normal state; for this reason I say that in the surgery of the epiglottis there is no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "throat hernia," and it is a large abscess in the color of a hazel, and it is very common in women; and it occurs according to two ways: natural and accident; or naturally there is no contrivance.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident occurs according to two ways, of which one is similar to fatty tumors, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from within a vein; and there is fear, and it should not be operated on by making cuts except in those that are small, and he proves and seeks out all the intervening parts: if you find it as fatty tissue and cannot distinguish it from any vein, you incise it as one would incise fat, and draw it to all its edges, if there is any; and seek well soon, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many manners of us are, of which I will say all the likenesses; and now it is fitting that I say all the difference which is between us and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is heat and fever holding on until the ebullitions have passed, and the putrefaction is accomplished; then the fever and heat cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	When the issue has neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains the syphix, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a swelling, and becomes large; and are according to two likenesses, or grease, or moist, and much of the color are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It must be, when you come to the treatment of the new wound, that you first examine and inquire about all the instrument called "intermissive," according to what its form will come or chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of inquiring about abscesses is that you search for or more moist part within the abscess, and turn your two instruments little by little, until you know that the instrument has reached the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the intermissive, and be careful lest it burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the moisture runs clear or of any color, cut it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after extracting the intermissive no more moisture comes out, know that it is fatty, so cut it crosswise, and remove it with forceps, and slightly cauterize each part. Watch where it lies, and treat the area around it soundly with the wound; and if you cannot treat it soundly, remove it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it remains nothing, it returns to us many times; and if there is a little of it, and the wound grieves, fill the wound with some corrosive powders, wet them, bind the wound, and place hot abscess-relieving things on it until it heals; and if the wound is large, suture the two edges of the wound, and treat those that nourish flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beating is contrary to you or some other thing hastens it, apply the vitriol powder, and let it lie for 2 or 3 days, until the wound rots, and rest the boiling of the blood; then return to the copper that which has remained from the new one.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the interposing instruments, and they are of three kinds: large, medium, and small. Among them, there are three square ones called "albaret," and one called "breb." These too come in three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses from fistulas. They are like the needles used for suturing threads, made of yellow brass or iron or silver. The yellow ones are more proven for encircling corruptions from fistulas. They also come in three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the perforations.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of the canine teeth are similar in appearance, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and among these canines there are those with two grooves in three ways; and there are those with three grooves, also in three ways; and there are those with two grooves, and some with only one groove, all of which are in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these for which they are used is the blade, and among those that cut only half the force, we cauterize the nose, because one does not puncture the vein nor the nerve; and from these are the instruments inserted into openings to prevent the patient from feeling during the incision of abscesses; and they are in three ways: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses no force with them in fleshier areas such as legs, arms, mammary glands, and angles, and similar places; and sometimes another instrument is made smaller, resembling shells of almonds, according to this form, for stopping bleeding.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed once in its place where it heals by degrees from the veins, and in the arteries, and once more according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, to such an extent that they appear like women's breasts; and remain ugly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them should do so according to this form from line .b. to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then cauterize the fat, and apply the wound with medicated charcoal, then sew the two edges of the wound together, and treat it until it heals; and if the breast hangs down and becomes soft due to its size as happens in women, cut into the rib above, by similar incisions; so that one edge is attached to the other at the end of each, with the larger line containing the vagina according to this form from line .b. to the line .g.; then cauterize the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment until it is healed; and if it is not healed or the incision is not fully done, because the patient does not wish to rest, or due to the flow of blood, you must fill the wound with moist cotton soaked in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the flesh and fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of arrow wounds
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from arrow wounds are similar to hard scrofula glands, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from the line b. to the line g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowe that is in the abscess is evacuated, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment appropriate for this until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula glands, incise it as we have said for incisions in scrofula, and if the wound contains bowe, apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured and the skin above is sewn together, there often develop abscesses. This also happens with a swollen vein and an abscess. If you recognize it to be due to the artery, the abscesses will be large and long-formed; and when you feel it with your hand, you sense the tension; and when it is due to the vein, it appears red and protruding; and it is foolish to attempt to lance such an abscess, especially when it is beneath the ribs, armpits, and other areas, and is very large.
