Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, one should avoid the iron cure, and in those who are chief, it is also advisable to avoid it. In those who are swollen from an artery, make a cut above the skin long enough; then perform the incision with forceps, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is fully exposed; then insert a needle, and pierce it all the way through to the other side, and clamp the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have taught you in extracting the two arteries in the temples. Then, introduce a foreign body between the two threads so that the fluid from inside escapes, thus relieving the abscess; then apply the cure appropriate for this situation until the clamps fall off; then treat with ointment suitable for such conditions until it is healed. If the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, you should tie your hand around the area where you can grasp some of the abscess, and insert a needle from your hand into the abscess, piercing it all the way through to the other side with the double thread as I have instructed; if you are unsure that the threads will hold, you should insert another needle under the entire abscess along the incision of the first needle, and clamp the threads in three places. Then, lance the abscess until the excess fluid escapes, then treat the skin for its superfluous parts and leave what is tied; finally, place a moist cloth with wine and oil on it, and apply bandages and ointments as needed until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come to the artery and vein, abscesses of the nerves when they are injured, or through too great labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in joints and bones in all places where there are joints, and it is the cause of abscesses, and its color seems like the color of the body, and is in many dispositions with pain; and when one restrains them forcefully, the patient feels great pain, and it is not just from within the body, but underneath the heart; and can be completely paralyzed, neither moving forward nor backward, neither down nor up, and that which is in joints should not be treated with iron: for fear of causing contraction; those on the head or forehead cause the skin to peel at the scalp.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and incise at its base; and if it is large, suspend it by a pin, cauterize it, then extract it and stitch the wound, and continue the treatment until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	No place except in the belly and nowhere else is it found, and it is a disease called "fungus" by its likeness to mushrooms, and it has fine roots and large heads; and there are both small and very large ones; and I have seen men who had two or more bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, with no difference, and were white, had fine roots, and were slightly cut, and in them there is constant moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other six [Z.], and the work in incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the artelul is white and moist and of subtle root; so cop it at the spatumile large, and let the cautery be at fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in the tailor, there are often too great discharges of blood, and if the skin breaks, then you must hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-made fine thread, and place it on the artelul as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then restrain it, and do not cease to strain the fine thread until it copes the artelul, and work thoroughly by it; and if the roots are large, you must fear to cop them immediately for the belly, but you may well cope half of them, then cauterize so that they do not return; then treat the wound, and guard that you do not cop the thelul which is of fugue color and of poor sense and with regard to milk.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess embedded, and I will come to the treatment of the chancre after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is hot
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from a fire cautery on a wound or a cut on the syface, and is on the belly with some of the boils, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what was mentioned before, or from windosity; and if it is by the rupture of the syface and by the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and is a light thing without pain, and obvious with various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more varied. When pressed at its roots, it rises and then returns. Sometimes it swells significantly upon entering the bath and due to great strain.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light matter, and clearly seen when you press with your hand; it does not constrain much. And if it is due to blood, it is clearly shown by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and inserted in a certain quantity; and if it is due to pneuma, it is swollen on touch, and the works are such that you observe whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or pneuma.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	You must let the treatment continue.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestines or the boil, you must instruct the patient to stretch his arm and extend it straight, then lance all around the belly; then command him to lie quietly between your hands, then go under the skin where you have lanced and pass through the entire length of the gush; afterwards, place half of the abscess extended above the ligature, and let your index finger rest on it; if you find it caught by the ligature, release it and return the intestine to the abdomen; and if you find the boil, take it with the needle and drain its excess; and if the artery opposes or the vein, pass directly through them, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, passing them in a cross where you made the piercing; then extract the abscess in four places above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the skin until it rots, and excise the dead flesh by itself; or you drain it when it is fine and rotten, then treat what needs to be treated, and close the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture you find, then treat the skin as needed, and suture the wound.
dou chancre	of the sore
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division of the signs of a sore, and how one should treat it with medicines, and how one should avoid the iron cure; and we say that sores often occur in the thighs, and great caution is needed in their treatment. The ancients said that when sores are on a part where they can be scraped, like those on the nipple, thigh, or similar parts, one must completely remove them when they are at the beginning; and when they are large and old, it is not advisable to approach them, for I have never seen any heal from such sores, nor have any healed before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when they are on a part where they can be removed, as we have said, are that you purge the patient once of black bile; then make him bleed if he has clear signs of excess, then prepare the patient for the operation by letting him lie well; then throw out the warts or sore, and the hair from all parts, and remove them completely without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and press your hand or something on the part to stop any bleeding contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, so cauterize until the bleeding stops; then continue with another cure until he is healed.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already discussed the signs of dropsy in division, and how the gathering of the water is made, and the signs of each sign, and the cure by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: it is only clarified; and one must not use iron in these two signs: namely, tympanites and hydrops, because they are mortal things; therefore when you treat this sign of dropsy called "eclites" by medicines, and the cure does not help, see if the patient is weak or has another disease besides dropsy, such as sudden relief from distension and similar conditions; then do not use iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient in good health, and he only has dropsy and is neither too thin nor too old, then proceed thus: hold the patient straight above your hands, and the attendants press the abdomen by directing the water to the lowest part of the foot, then take the thorny spatium according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let the point be such that it does not enter too deeply so that it cannot reach the intestines when inserted, and cannot be closed; then look to see if the hydrops is located near the intestines: in this case, you must incise above the belly three cuts directly under the knife. And if the hydrops is due to liver disease, let your cut be on the left side of the belly three cuts; and if it is due to the mesentery, let it be on the right, and it is not fitting that the patient lie on the incision so that the superfluous fluids do not flow to the weak part. Then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push out, and raise your hand to remove all the spatillum between the skin and the sifac as if scraping in quantity of a nail or slightly less. Then pierce the sifac until the spatillum comes to the right place, and this is the passage for the water, then draw it out, and let this instrument have the form described here.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a thin silver needle, made of light brass or iron, and placed under the part below the small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on the other side, and one on another; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the form of the incision that writers cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	Above the head is the alemele, such that when the instruments come to the edge, they now go slightly above the instrument; empty it then half or a third part, for if you empty more than it should in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he falls senseless, or he nears death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then withdraw the instrument and retain the edge, and it is retained now for the cork that plugs the hole which I spoke of, that you pierce in this manner; then reapply the instrument on another day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw a little fluid; do this any day, and take care not to follow too much until it no longer remains but just a bit of fluid.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the patient, and leave much fluid, cure it with heat from burial earth or sand, and by much sweat or bath and in the sun, and make him drink; cure of medicines desiccative until it is healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of the fluid, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping up of the urethra
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born who does not have pores in the urethra, or where the pores are small, or are not in their proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it suits him to do so quickly before he passes much very subtle mucus according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place or pierce the small lead of plumb and bind it and keep it thus three days or four and when it wants to make urine, remove the closes and let urine flow, and then put it back; and by chance it may not be necessary at all, for the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the wound from which the lead is pierced is small, it should be medicated with a lead clove, as we have said, and it will enlarge.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the wound in their place are bledder, for none are born with the wound at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis upwards; and they cannot void because the matter cannot come down to the bladder, and this is a harmful illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the patients lie often on their back, then the head of the verge and the cope are made as the size of a feather's tail, so that the perforations are each in the middle, as it should be; and beware of the flow of blood which comes many times, and if it happens, stop it with what stops blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the verge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times these abscesses come in the verge, and they are an appearance of foul flesh; and among them there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must treat them with a sharp lancet, and lance and cleanse all of them, then place soft cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then dress with clarifying ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the ulcer is malignant, of putrid color and emitting pus, then you must apply a cauterization to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	And when you have excised it, and if the ulcer is on the verge, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then you must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is sutured, you treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all together, it is not assured that the head of the shoulder will not be pierced, and black rot and corruption come to the verge and wound; then you must remove all that is black and corrupt, and then bind with a plaster made from the bark of pomegranate peel and viper's flesh, and treat with other dressings until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery aids in two dispositions together: that is to say, in bleeding and in corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then it is necessary that you insert a probe into the penis and let the patient urinate through it; and when the hair is shaved at the head of the penis which comes to those who have not been circumcised, or where there is a wound or abscess, then it must be that you cauterize around the base of the penis and foreskin until the ligaments are released, and release the head of the penis from all sides; and if this is a serious matter to discuss with someone, then it must be that you cauterize around a little part of the base of the penis and skin with a cautery tip; then separate thoroughly between two, and place a fine linen cloth moistened in cold water over it again.
de la circoncision	of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not an incision of continuity like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this work out of our own volition, and properly on infants, it is necessary that we do the best work and the most gentle for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have it only what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the majority of masters and practitioners who performed circumcision using forceps, and with a single scalpel; they often cut too deep because there are two layers, and by accident one cuts through the upper layer and remains in contact with the lower one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is difficult, and the pain is doubled, and in the dressing which is from without the point of the limb is not assured; and in the dressing of the nail by accident the iron escapes, and the work runs amok, and many times they arise thus without needing a dressing and I have seen it so.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the dressing which is done with force on all the thread of hair I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the force cuts just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press with your hand, you cut equally all around the entire thread; but that the hairs be very thin underneath the skin; and let the manner of the first operation be such that you make the child, if it hears, think that you are only loosening the hair around the shaft merely, and let him perceive in every way that you can; then hold it straight between your hands, and place the forces between your hands or under your feet that the child cannot see, nor any of the instruments; then put your hand to the shaft and blow or cough, and draw it up until the head of the shaft is fully enclosed; then dress well with the filth which has accumulated, then bind the upper signet with a double thread, then bind underneath bit by bit; and hold it on the right side at the second hour in your pocket and indicate to the right hand, and cope between the two bonds, then lift the cork quickly and draw the head of the shaft; then let the blood trickle slowly, for this is the best; and put powder over and over the powder with a piece of cloth stuck on with raw egg white, confected with rose oil well and fresh, and leave it on until another day, and cure with other dressings until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of force for the circumcision is this: the two shoulders should be tied and sharp, and the shoulders should be as large as the hands equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in circumcision is when the corners inside go beyond the incision; therefore, you must stretch them with your finger, just as the corners are made for an abscess; and the flap equally, and if you cannot hold it with your finger, hold it with forceps, and then fold it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they protrude three days, and what is below the penis swells, you must leave it until the abscesses are appeased, and gently brand it; fold the flap as much as you can, and avoid the part of the penis, for it will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the head of the sudden wound from powder things, as we have said in treating powders, and if one copes too much from the heart, and it goes above, it will not harm; cure it therefore, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	retain the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of a stone, or congealed blood, or a bow, or new flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not relieved, and you see that the retention is caused by the stone which is at the neck or base of the bladder, then it must be that the patient lies on his knees; and extend his belly from the part above the back, and restrain the patient as much as he can; and thus the necks of the bladder are constrained to the expression of the stone above, for which reason the urine is relieved. And if it does not come, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which here is its form: and let it be of fine silver, light and slender like a bird's feather; and let its handle be half a palm long, and slender at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of issuing urine is that you take a double thread and tie it at the end to a bit of wool or cotton, and put the head of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and fill the head of the syringe until it is full, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and wipe his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis, so that it comes to the root of the penis, then cover the penis from above towards the mouth; then fill the syringe before until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel the urine coming until the thing is empty, and this is not done according to this order because the guide where it goes is crooked; then pull the thread little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it out, and make the urine flow; and refill the syringe as long as the bladder is emptied, and bind the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come into the bladder, or putrefaction is gathered there, and you see it discharge acidic fluids and medicines, then make all the instrument called "clepsydra," and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; the leashes are placed so that the medicines may be well infused into the urethra to anesthetize it thoroughly. Thus, when moisture needs to be drawn out or added, place the head of the tube in the moisture, then draw it through the tract which is there; by drawing the moisture through the tube and then firmly reinserting it, the moisture will enter the tract and reach the bladder, allowing the patient to feel it. This is the form of the subtle enema used to treat the bladder: as follows:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or steel, and the head is higher; and beneath the breast where the ligaments fall; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture you wish to clarify the bladder with inside it, then join the two breasts forming a single double thread, and heat that bit of moisture on the fire; then insert the head of the catheter into the urethra, then squeeze your hand over the bladder until all the moisture is delivered as needed, so that the patient feels the moisture has arrived in the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly through; then insert the strong thread into these perforations, then assemble the circle as one assembles the handle, and put inside what you wish of oil and moisture and water, and join it in the instrument; do so as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture appears in the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the division the methods of stones, and their extraction together with medicines; and we have said the difference between a stone forming in the bladder and all the signs, and which stone one should operate on in size; and in the bladder, and in the vein; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often to children, and this is a sign that the urine has jumped from the bladder seeming like urine in its subtlety; and it clearly hardens, and gradually weakens the patient's vein, and pierces him many times, and then constricts; and most of these jumps are at the foundations; and the cure is lighter for children until they are four years old, and it is much more serious in older people, and is medium for those between childhood and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it must first cleanse the patient with a clyster to remove all the filth from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it obstructs at times when seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, and draw them out and move them into place so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and exits once from above; then have the patient sit between your prepared hands, and their hands be under their thighs, so that the bladder hangs entirely downward; then press and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, now hasten to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not descend upon touching the entire area, soften your index finger of the left hand, if the patient is pregnant, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and fully formed; then place your hand on its foundation, press the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, move it to the neck of the bladder; then press above your finger, and cut at the place where you see it should be cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upward, and remove the skin that is beneath the ribs in the part where the incision is made; then he inserts the spatule cutting, from which this is formed.
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make the incision between what is between the ribs and the pelvis, not in the middle but on the side of the left inguinal region; and be straight over the stone, and your two hands should be close to or near the pelvis, and make the incision so that it is wide at the front and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance, press the hand that is near the pelvis until it breaks without much effort; know that there are stones with angles and edges: they are easier to remove; and some are round like a gland, and smooth, from which the removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those who have angles and margin, make the size greater; and if it does not fit, you must clamp with tongs that are like a file at the head, to move and extract the stone so it does not escape; or you pour under the instrument a subtle curved tube at the head; and if you cannot fit it thus, you enlarge the hole a bit, and if it is uncleaned, you extract it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, you pour first the larger one into the neck of the bladder, then cover up, then pull hard, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, you must sew it up, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out through it so that the veins cannot be sewed up; but nevertheless strive to treat it, or break it with tongs, as you remove it piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, cover the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, and extract it, and place a moist cloth over it in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then reswaddle the patient for three days without unbinding the bandage.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate it, raise the head of the bone very well with oil and water, then treat with an ointment of defluxicon and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses and corruptions of blood in the bladder, and retention of urine due to these, which is known in such a manner that it moves with the urine: then pour your thumb into the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder; then wash the wound with water and oil and salt, and help it in all ways you see until it is healed; and it must be that whenever you treat these wounds, you bind both thighs and apply the medicines to the bone.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the urethra, and urine cannot pass; you should cut as I have said before, but this cutting may be excused due to the procedure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already proven this in such a manner.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take I iron fork according to this form and fix it in the fire with three angles.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and place it around the urethra below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the fork gently into the urethra until it reaches the stone; and turn the fork in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from another side; then urine will come forth soon. Then press your hand above what remains of the stone inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is broken soon and jumps with urine, the patient recovers; and if you cannot do this for any reason, tie one thread under the stone and another above, then place the needle at the stone between the two threads, extract it forcefully, untie the thread, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and treat until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Often it happens that a stone is formed in women, and if this happens even once, the wound must be treated carefully, and it is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who can disclose herself to mirrors, especially when she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that sometimes it cannot be found a woman well knowing this art by hand; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is more imperfect than the man's stone, for which reason it must be made a deeper cut, and great fear arises. And if necessity demands this from those, then you must seek a well-knowing midwife, and find her among the people, and if you do not find one, at least find a very subtle substitute; and she should present a safer way in women's lives, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to perform what you command regarding the inquiry of the stone; and look very carefully if the woman is a virgin: then it must be that she puts forth her root and seeks the stone; and if she finds it, constrain her under her root, and recommend that she put forth her root or concomitantly with the patient, and seek and press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, it must be moved gradually from the entrance of the bladder down to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then cut into the stone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the groin, arrange your hand where it appears, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your finger over or under the stone, and let the incision be at first small; then insert the pincers into the incision, if you feel the stone make the wound larger so that the stone can exit fully, and know that there are many kinds of stones: namely, small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you know the signs to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the vein bursts, put vitriol powder on it and hold it for an hour until the swelling subsides; then return to your work until the stone is removed, and have the tools I said in the extraction of the stone ready for those who help you with your work; and if the vein bursts, and this is from the artery that has been cut, put powder on it and bind it tightly with bandages, and do not repeat this step, and leave the stone alone and do not treat it further, lest the patient dies suddenly; then dress the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is relieved, and the swelling subsides, then return to your work until the stone is removed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fatty hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aquouse rheum is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white vitreous humor, which is beneath the heart of the embryo, containing the egg; and it is called "vitreous humor," and sometimes it is truly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks it is another egg; and it is the skin of the embryo between the white vitreous humor as we have said; and this does not happen often.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this rheum is due to weakness that comes to the embryos, and this material is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from percussion on the embryos, and this moisture has many colors: it may be yellowish, or without red, or black, or white watery, and this happens more often; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white vitreous humor as we have said, it is a true abscess, though long and similar in shape to an egg, yet it does not burst the embryos, for it is moist all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper cloth, the abscess is treated with a part of the egg, and because of this, one thinks it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the quill and the white surface, one feels it well; therefore when you wish to know the color of the moisture, you test through the intervening square, of which the form is described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intervening square, judge of what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with iron, the patient must be bled according to our power and the fullness of his body; then place the sponge on his back, on one thing somewhat high, and put a layer of wool over him; sit on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit on his right, extending the rod to one of the two ribs of the quill of the quill. Then take the spatula flat, and scrape the skin of the quill among them long until near the blade, and make the slit entirely straight by dividing the skin of the quill up to the white part, and slightly cauterize it according to your power; then pierce the white full of water with a large perforation, and drain all the water, and then apply your pins, and raise the white upward; and do not touch the heart of the quill, but only the white; scrape everything or in pieces very finely so that if you do not scrape it well, the water will return; and if the egg has failed in your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white; then sew the two flaps of the heart of the quill with a seam, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it must be that you tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the flow of blood; then cauterize the ion along the entire suspension, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the humor is gathered in two parts joined together, know that these are two branches; then cauterize the other part as you did the first equally, and wipe away the blood, and put in the wound moistened wool in rose oil; and place another moistened wool in wine and oil, and place over the two ions, and put above folded cloths, and tie it all according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded wool according to this likeness and stitch them at the waistband of the trousers. One head of the shoulder is placed on the fundament down to the back, and the other to the part near the knife. The other heads are placed over the two angles, and all is stitched together in the loop of the trousers. This branch is often treated with a fire cautery instead of iron tongs, and you should use the sharp surgical cautery. Remove the skin from the ions, and heat them as we have said, so that the white fat containing the humor is revealed. Then take the cautery according to this form, and prick that white fat with the needle points, and sear it with this sharp hot cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And you apply the hot iron in all ways that you can, until you wither it completely; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more salve; and move guards against hemorrhage, and cure the incisions; and if anything contrary to you happens, or abscesses or hemorrhages or other things, then treat what happens contrary to you according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this work because of its horror, then perform perforation as I have said. For when you are certain by the signs that we have mentioned that an abscess is present, make the sick person sit on a raised seat; pierce the abscess in the part beneath all the way to the large space, and place the perforation along the length of the body; let the openings be wide so that all the fluid may flow out. Then put cotton at the site and bind it, allowing the remaining fluid to drain, and treat the wound until it heals. If the white cloth does not allow the fluid to exit through the opening of the wound, you must insert a pen or the instrument used to drain fluid from dropsy patients, as described before; widen the opening of the wound, and know that the fluid will return and gather after about six months or so. When it has gathered as described, then the patient's days will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the roots
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	In the section of this branch there is fear in many preparations, which is why it seems to me that we should leave it as it is; and I will tell you the procedure and similar matters concerning the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come from flesh, and especially from the roots; and it is by much chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say that abscesses come from bitter and acrid superfluity, which spreads to the roots, or through percussion; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the flesh; and it does not find any pain, and is a grievous abscess; and by chance it may be a painful and stony abscess, with fugitive color, and sometimes comes from a vein, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, it is known by the disposition of a hot abscess, when you press on both sides; and it is not fitting that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Who is made from venous swelling is known by its disposition at the expression of the touch of both sides, and can indeed cut well on this resemblance and on other marks; and you peel the core of the apple, then the seed is at the top, and the tail tough of the white soft, and release the suspender from all sides of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is hardened with these marks present, then you must incise the egg and peel it; and if it is dry at the soft part, or in what is inside the vessels, then you must release all that taint, and peel it thoroughly.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess from the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess wrapped in a wrapping that resembles a borjon, with the groin softened. The patient experiences severe pain as it changes; and the treatment for this disease is well-preserved similarly to what was mentioned before. We will detail the work for this according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It must be that you place the patient on an elevated seat, then put the suspender of the groin over your two shoulders, down to all the vessels close to the groin, and make them hold the masters tightly, stretching them thoroughly; then cut with a sharp spoon-like instrument across the vessels so they are uncovered, and then scrape from each part as we have said in the extraction of arteries in temples; then insert a needle where it has the double thread, and fix it at the first place where the vein came out, and again at another place; then sew in the middle straightly, according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted moistures; then treat the wound as with others when you incise them, so that no vessel chievements which nourish one of the groins; for by this there is no harm, and if at all the vessels come forth veins, it must be to take out the groins from all the vessels; so that the testicles do not lose their nourishment due to incision of the vessels, dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syphax
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrences of this branch are by section that comes from the rupture of the syphax, or from extension in the abdomen at the part of the ingers, for which reason the intestine descends from that rupture to one of the ilia; and this rupture is either of the syphax, or of the extension of it, and come about by these two manners of causes: by percussion, or jumping, or shouting, or lifting a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the syphax are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are even until near the middle, for this reason that the syphax presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is from the section of the ileum, that it causes a sudden onset of pain, and various abscesses appear beneath the skin, for the discharge of the intestine and the body below the ileum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the cicatrices with the intestine are retained inquisitively, and cause great pain to the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron causing fear, for which it is advisable to avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement;
