aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the work is that you command or patient to retract the intestine inside the wound with his hand if it can enter; then anoint it at its root and lift the thighs. Then place the keir above, and peel all the skin from the length; then insert the leivers of the thigh uncines according to what you need to open the wound, making sure they are such that the oesophagus could issue forth; then cauterize the ileum that is beneath the skin lengthwise until the white ileum hard is discovered on all sides; then place your index finger in what follows the coccyx, between the white ileum which is beneath the skin of the egg, and between the second ileum, and depart what is behind the egg, and between the second ileum; and then move with your right hand inside the keir of the coccyx, and place the white ileum high in your left hand, and lift the egg towards all the ileum away from the spine; and command the minister to extend the egg upwards, and release what is behind the ligament; and wait with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine enveloped or hard ileum, and if you find anything, put it back into the belly beneath; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten threads, and insert it in the rear part of the ileum, which is after the skin of the coccyx; behind the spine, then peel the heads that appear from the threads until there are four threads; then assemble them one above the other in the manner of a cross, and fasten the ileum, which we said was beneath the skin of the coccyx, with a strong thread of two fingers' breadth; then wrap the heads of the threads, and tie firmly with two strands, so that no vessels that nourish them can enter into it, lest an abscess form; and reinsert the thread according to the first long thread, and after these two threads leave the ileum which is beneath the keir of the coccyx the size of a finger's breadth; then continue all the rest according to the roundness that the egg bears; then apply moistened wool in oil, and put it on the wounds, and administer the thread as we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the whites of the eyes are cauterized to prevent bleeding after incision due to doubt.

For this often happens, and leave the thread until it draws by itself; and if it delays in falling out, it should be soaked in hot water, and then follow what we have said until it draws; then treat the wound with another dressing until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of fatty hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this case, I have never known anyone to dare treat it with iron.

And the ancients said that it is made like the wire that is wound together at the vis, in such a manner that you tie the vessels, after cutting lightly on the dislocation; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of those who work, until the vessels constrict; and treat it as we have said until it is perfectly healed.

Sometimes there is a rupture in the veins, as we have said, and the eyes become apparent; and no parts of the intestines protrude at the seams, and if they do, it is little and retracts every hour; and yet, if it remains too long in this spot, the wound or syphacul may form because the intestines protrude; and this happens due to the stretching of the syphacul that is in the veins, as we have said, for it stretches, then softens and swells the eyes and becomes apparent; and the cure is by fire cauterization, as we have previously said; and sometimes the wound is cured by iron in this manner: and it is when the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then take the eye of the rupture swollen from the large according to the size of three nails; and then extract the syphacul that is beneath the skin that follows, then take the reed and place it over the apparent eye of the syphacul; and press it well against the belly, then suture the two eyes of the syphacul above the head of the reed, and suture one and the other; then extract the head of the reed, and do not cover the syphacul nor extend the eye or any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the ramification of the intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The seam is constrained, and shows no sign in the rupture, and the cauteries are healed in this place, and closer to safety.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the cheeks
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the cheeks is softened in some people, because the flesh inside is softened, and it can be seen; when one wishes to treat this, the patient should lie on their back, and the softened skin should be cut from the natural skin. dou chastrement	by just punishment
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Skeith that chastremens is escomeniez in nostre loi, and for ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; and n’est necessaires fuer that por II manieres: of which the one is that li mires en saiche respondre when on li demandera, and en saiche la cure; and the other, por ceu that nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastremens is done according to two manners: either by attraction or by breaking.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do by attraction, make the beast sit in hot water until the joints are softened and warm. Then hold them with your hand until they are set and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castration: it is fitting that you castrate the beast, and squeeze the sack with your left hand, then tie up the suspender, and cut above each testicle one cut, when you will have well scorched them; and I leave a little bit of soft fat which is under the vessels; and this way of castration is better than that made by attraction, for in attraction there may accidentally remain something from the sack, by which the beast desires lust; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodites are according to two manners in men: one is that between the two testicles it appears as the figure of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in the middle there is urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other method is for women, placed above the knife as a rod and two coins.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you clean all the wounds thoroughly, and treat them as other wounds; in the second manner, for those whose urine flows through the skin of the scrotum, they do not require any treatment.
de la tentigene	of the beard
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentigene is a wound on the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have them as large as a hand, and this is how they are treated.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must dye the excess of the tentigene with your hand or needle and treat it lightly; and do not overdye it too much, lest blood flow. Treat it with other remedies until it heals; and for another wound that appears at the opening of the vein, cover it and perhaps it will rupture, resembling a cow's udder, and because of this they called it in ancient times "cow disease.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must cut it, as we have said regarding the tumor and its treatment until it is healed.
de erratique	of erratic
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic if it is when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the perforation is small; and it is natural by birth, or an accident caused by illness that comes; or it is due to excess of heat, or too much or too little spiciness, and is made perfect in the thighs, or sides, or beneath, or wherever it may be; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and sometimes the flowers to have; and the knowledge of these things is by the look of the urine.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swellings are near and apparent, seek with your fingers or touch them.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a sharp syphilis and near the two flanks, hasten, and treat as follows: bring your two index fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two flaps, so that the subtle syphilis is removed, and over the stumps; then take wool, and the fat in oil, and put it on the wound, and lie with the woman each day, so that it does not scab.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the syphilis is hard and thick, it is necessary to scrape with a spatula resembling a bay leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stumps are of live flesh, suspend them with an oncine and scrape; and use hemostatic medicines such as acetia, dragon's blood, incense, together abundant egg whites; then administer a broad strip of lint, so that the wound does not scab; and thus keep it long, and give him another linen tent; then continue to dress until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a carbuncle brings forth pus, it should be treated according to this method, unless it is an encrusted abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an encrusted abscess in the carbuncle, one should not touch it to incise.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that without cause commonly occur. And when hemorrhoids are old, they become thrombosed; and we have already mentioned the similar cases of auscultation, and the signs, and I will now say those that can receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombosed ones, when they are fully ripe in the carbuncle, do not appear by touch; except those cured with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the sore, which one can feel, are those one can treat.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should place the woman in a cold room, then put the altelul in the tongs, and the copa in its roots, then sprinkle medicines that restrain blood, such as myrrh, dragon's blood, and incense, and similar things; then place her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding continues, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranate peel and garlic and similar things, and then take flour of barley, and mix it with honey and garlic, and apply a plaster to her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, if you cause it to draw suction cups on the back and breasts without piercing; then take wool, and mix in grease with juice of plantain or of agnus castus with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess rests, cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, so it must be treated as I have said for the thigh; and then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of abscesses of the arm
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses occur in the arm, such as chancre, porous abscess, herpes, estiomenes, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must say in this treatise on the hot abscess that comes from the arm, which is not one of those abscesses that swell suddenly; and if you wish to know the procedure, observe whether the abscess has begun its appearance, and is full of heat and fever, and becomes red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce it but let it die until the pain is appeased; and then place the patient on a seat, and have two small seats or stools for him to recline, and support his back and align his feet with the parts below the leg; and spread his thighs, and place his arms beneath his knees, and tie them well with a good bandage; then apply the bale from the right side, and lead it to the instrument used for the mouth of the arm, of which we will speak later in form; and it must be that when you see this instrument being applied, you insert the probe first to know the depth of the arm, so that what enters into the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instruments are larger, it must cover the depth of the arm with cloths, so that the instrument does not weigh on him; and it must place the horn of the instrument above, and test the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened, and one makes it soft by hand, it must be covered at the head, at the spatillum light; and when the bow [pus] is evacuated, you must put in the wound moistened cloths in rose oil, or in green vitriol oil; and place the cloth out of the wound on the margin of the sore, and put above the sore and above the blade clean moistened linen in water or honey be cooked; then cure after two days anointing suitable for this, until it is healed; and sometimes lift the sore and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then of water or roots of lily and long pepper be cooked; then return to the anointing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is placed on the margin, you must take care to avoid cauterizing with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Mestier is first in labor when she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman push avidly, and desire to breathe: then hasten the birth of the child; then know that this childbirth is according to the natural figure, and comes headfirst with the second coming after it; and when you see these signs, you should gently press her abdomen, so that the child comes out quickly; for when he descends on his head, the second follows after it, and is cleansed of its impurities by good cleansing. And who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For he comes sometimes on his feet, and comes forth into the body or the shoulder, and the hands, or where he comes on her abdomen, or side, and is turned by chance over his neck, and in other bad figures; it is necessary for labor that she be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should aid them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes upon his head through natural birth, and the woman delivers easily, and the virtue of her is weak, then let it sit on a saddle, or where women hold it; and arise from its nature, oil or fenugreek being cooked, then pour the balm between its two little spatumiles as they are formed.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and cut the second nerve, and let it lie until the moisture that is within comes out; and press her abdomen so that the child descends. If it does not descend, then clisterize the woman with fenugreek muscilage and safflower oil. Then make her drink and sneeze of condisi, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands emerge broken, you must gently reduce them little by little; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on the seat, and lift her feet up high; then remove the seat from the ground, and support the woman so she does not scream during the reduction; and if the hands cannot be reduced and the child dies, cut off the hands with the knife that is mentioned before, and extract the child, reducing them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child at his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes at his feet, you must lift him up; and then turn him little by little until he is equal; then take his feet and extend them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to the hips, then command him to hold back, and make him sneeze by tickling his nose; if it is feverish, let God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not feverish as we have said, turn it little by little, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it does not come to fever as we have said, take musk of almond, oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind them all in a mortar; then put the nature of the woman inside and above this ointment, and let her sit in warm water until below the ribs; when she is softened below, give her myrrh to wear, and place it under her, and let her have it for an hour; then let her sit on the stool, and tickle her nose and mouth, and gently rub her abdomen, for the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the issue from the child above his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, put your hands gently on him little by little; then rub his neck, and let his feet hang down, and lie him on the bed; bend his hands little by little, and then place his hands over his abdomen, removing the cushions beneath until he is supported below; and if the child does not move, take his feet and shape them firmly, then raise his abdomen upwards, and put your hands in; and lift the child little by little; and command the woman to hold on tightly until the child passes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the issue of the child which comes with one hand wide open
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must devise to bring back the hand: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand and walk; if she cannot walk, lay her on the bed and prop up her legs firmly; then apply the ligature as I have recounted; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the chair, then study to bring back the hand; and take the child according to its natural position, and make her sneeze, and command her to grip until the infant is forced out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	From the birth of the child at its neck, and have spread its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I must have the child grasp its hand, then turn it little by little, and gently; and when it is equal, place on the natural ligature of vein and oil as we have said, then command her to move it little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on the chair, and command her to grip; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for all the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for all the secondine, cut the secondine with your finger until the moisture is evacuated; and if the infant can fit on its face and on its neck, cut from the mouth, so that it is not retained, and kill the infant; then put the child inside, as much as you have placed it, and instruct the woman to bear it only once: then gently extract it.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the issue of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins often are born, and sometimes three or four are born; this is not an uncommon thing, and it rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are extracted things, and do not live much, if at all; I know them, that they be multiplied, and are devised by the syphilis which is linked to the bowels; and sometimes issued also naturally like unto worms, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue smoothly, the treatment as we have said, and let the bile subtle flow quickly and easily; do so as it benefits for healing.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to fifteen, and are all formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the glorious sage, and it should be that the bile know all this, for similar things may happen; do so according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the mother of the dead child or her womb as I have said in the division, and there is no discharge, and you are forced to perform manual work; then you must know if the woman is healthy and has no accidents or fear of death. She should be soothed on her back, with her head inclined forward, and her legs raised. The minister should place her hands on two parts, tying her to the bed such that she is not moved for the descent of the child. Then, rub her mouth with moist oils mixed with muscilage of althea and fenugreek, and linseed oil. Anoint her hands with these oils and muscilages lightly, then place the palms in the mortar where you have prepared the oncin. Ensure that the child is positioned to descend onto its head; if the descent is through the feet, insert the oncin or a pin along the mid-back. The oncin should be placed in her right hand, and she should hold it between her left index finger and thumb. She should gently place this in any of the areas we have mentioned until it reaches an empty space; this is the form of the oncin.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then prick against the other pin, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions be equal; and then stretch equally by moving back and forth, to allow issuance, and let the pins have teeth to hold them, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, and he wags any of his eyes, and places them in that part, and draws out the other part; and if there remains nothing, then set this pin or higher up, and do this until it is all drawn out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be brought back by squeezing, then you must wrap it with a cloth, until it is all drawn out; then bind it at the joint of the sole or on the cut, and do this likewise for the other hand, and for both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and the birth canal is narrow, or it has a sharp obstruction, you must place the spineless spatumile between your hands, make an incision in the head, and extract the sharp obstruction; or you can use a tool called "almidach", which comes with the instruments or chapter after this one; and then similarly, let the child have a large natural head; and then pull the bones out with forceps, and if the head must be cut, do so to the extent that the obstructions are released; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the back, you must pierce it until the obstructions flow.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is under its feet, the traction is light, and the direction to the mouth of the birth canal is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is narrow in the belly or at the nipple, it must be extracted with a flytrap enveloped on the hand; and make the belly or the nipple as wide as the moist substance that is present; and if the other limb has been removed, and the head remains, he should apply honey to its palm thoroughly; then he should cut up to the mouth of the honey; afterwards, he should pour in one or two ounces, and pull out; and if the mouth of the honey has become narrow due to a hot abscess that has come there, it is not fitting to work on it, but it must be given moist and greasy things; and he should apply plasters, and a compress in water softening and moistening.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the injury is on his side, and you can set it equal, apply what we have said for the living child; and if one has no power, cut out with forceps piece by piece, and leave nothing of the secondine.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the one that we said comes to be in the abscesses that come from the gums; and if bleeding occurs, it should be put in cold water restraining, and give him other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose belly an infant had died, then I sutured the other [one] over it, and prevented the death of the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed in the mouth, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for the treatment, and I thought long about it, and could not staunch the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a plaster with strong吸引力，从中取出了一块骨头，之后几天又取出了其他一些。
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvelled much, for the belly has no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I examined the wound and found bones there, as the woman improved significantly; and the woman lay long thus, with a bit of blood from the vein; and I did not remember this chapter for the reason that when masters find an unfamiliar thing, they must know how to provide aid.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to reset the dislocation to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	After that comes the form of the presser, to which one writes in the books; and twice around the two heads of the bones.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	In every way, the horns should be more subtle from the restrictoire, and made of ebony or boxwood; and let the mouth of the fust be two fingers wide, and the margin of the trees one palm and a half long; in between the two limbs there should be two attachments of this same wood, firmly set in each, half a palm or a bit longer in length; and these two attachments are inserted into the mouth of the maris to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of pliers; and let it have two heads, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you wish to open the maris with all the instrument, place the woman on the bed, her feet hanging and legs spread, then insert the two attachments together into the maris, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then work your hand on the entire instrument as you did with the pliers equally, according to the amount you wish to open the mouth of the maris until the hinge does what it wills.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is entirely mounted, and its images are multiplied; and when the user has them prepared, it is more rapid in its work, and higher for men due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not use the instrument properly unless it is prepared, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained during childbirth, it must be instructed to grip her abdomen, and then cause her to sneeze gently. And if she passes it through this means, well and good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, take a spoon or cover and put herbs that can open the mouth of the child inside, such as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cayenne, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or steeped in water on fire. Then place one end of the spoon or cover in the mouth of the child, and hold it until the vapors enter the child's mouth; then cause her to sneeze as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint moves quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and is not able to be moved, command the maid to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or muscilagin of althea, then put the bottle back in nature, and seek the second joint; and when she has found it, take it and extend it little by little straight, so that the tendons do not chafe at the extraction; but she must move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then draw; it will come and be disengaged.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the tendon is tightly chafed, we have said the treatment for sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not from all that we have said, then guard that you do not proceed rashly in drawing; but it must be that what is at the mouth of the tendon, that you bind it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with a tetrapharmcon ointment enema; she will take it and put it back, and it will become able to move. But still, when she takes it, if it produces an不良气味 to the stomach and head, and causes the patient discomfort.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If therefore suitable fumigations are required for this: some of the ancients have proven the fumigation of cress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman for the retention of flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass resembling a cane, and one places the fine end in the nature, and the wide heads above the fire; and let the fumigations be upon the coals, and the scab until it is corroded, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the foundation pierced, but have a softened one with a syfac: therefore it is necessary for the baile to pierce that syfac in the right place, and not the spatumile itself sharply, and guard the lacement so that she does not touch it; then place upon moistened wool in wine and oil, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not close, put or hold a plug of lint, and let it remain in place, and be removed when the child seems ready to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this plug comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it must be handled suddenly: if it needs to be treated, as we have said for the lint plug.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula of the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the fundament are nodules, and grow larger than those that come from leakage of the fundament or in the space between two parts, resulting in one fistula or multiple; and when this nodule is old, it works, and often contains moisture, a white or fine pus, and sometimes these fistulas are Persian; they are known by those who have them through evacuation or windiness when the patient evacuates, and by chance during a passing of wind.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they reach fistulas to the bladder, and to the half of the penis; and reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula penetrating to the fundament, and not penetrating: and it is that you place your index finger in the fistula, and insert a fine needle of steel or iron when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, insert a fine probe of linen, or horsehair, as long as you feel the probe or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no discharge from the fistula nor windiness nor flatulence as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; so hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is pierced to the bladder or to the urethra, it will discharge urine, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	And if it is pierced to the hip joint, the tent will come just to its place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of pain in between, then it is such that it returns to its place, and neither medicine nor immediate healing by ointment is worth anything; and in these pierced fistulas, there is no cure other than labor and the vanity of foolish practitioners who undertake them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	And in that which is neither pierced nor ancient, for hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on his back; and the servant lifts the legs up to his hips, and bends his hips toward his belly; then set a tent of iron or of ploughshare if there is tortuosity, as much as you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain deep within the buttocks, you must place your index finger there; if you then feel that the vein has been pierced, know that it is a vein; do not work on it much as it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can treat well with aid only some cases, but this happens rarely; the help that one applies, consists in heating the cautery to a subtle degree according to the size of the fistula, as was previously said; and you insert it hot into the fistula until it comes from the buttocks; do this two or three times, until you know that the threads are thoroughly burned, which resemble bird feathers; then dress with wet cloths in butter until the threads have come out, then dress with ointment, healing the flesh and closing the wound.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus set, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus set, otherwise it cannot be set. And if the arrowhead is between and does not penetrate just to the root which is the foundation, and you place a thick covering of flesh or sponge between your finger and the arrowhead, and you see the fistula at the part where the covering is taken off; scrape from the beginning of the fistula, and apply something before the arrowhead, and cauterize after it until it reaches the tip of the arrowhead; then the arrowhead will be delivered and fall out. Then clean those flesh parts that seem like a bird's feather, leaving none remaining.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the seton fails and cuts between you and the wound, cauterize with fire or medicinal water.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauteries bring together two good things: that is to say, the burning of these wounds, and the stopping of blood and drying of moisture; then treat the wound with ointments soothing hard flesh, and are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is sound and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the point of the fundament and is distant from the body, touch or place your finger at the fundament, and inquire it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the wound and between them is cloth or syphage or wounds, and it is about to pierce through, if there be no way of hope and expectation, by administering one of the three methods: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut to the bottom, or if you can, put ointments and treat as first; and do not go too close to the point of piercing, lest you cut the tissue that holds the fundament, and cause the discharges by its own will; then treat as we have said; by chance it may be healed, or you remove that covering and clean since it is cut from beneath the fundament with a tent or other pointed instrument; then cleanse the necessary flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound and to arrest the fistula above the fundament: this will be a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are treated in this manner: and it is when you poke the tent into the fistula, and it is located near the base beneath the skin, so take a perforated tent from the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And you poke the thread into two turns, and push the tent onto all the thread in the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perianthic near the margin of the base inside, then extract the thread from that perforated one, as you poke your finger or base; and pull the tip of the thread, and join the two heads together, and hold them against each other, and let them be for one or two days; and hold them only once, until the threads close the gaps between them completely; then treat the wound until it is healed and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, make it perforate in all ways that you can, provided it is not too close to the surface.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not fitting to cauterize for the ligature if too close to the surface, and then treat, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spatumile spine from which the fistula is made is very jagged on one side and sharp; and on the other side not so much, because what should not be cauterized should not be cauterized, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are in two ways: some are within the rectum, like grains of resin, and they can be small or large, often accompanied by blood, with one or more; they are outside the rectum and at the anus. But those outside have little moisture and only a slight amount of yellowish water or blood, maintaining the color of the body. For those within the rectum, instruct the patient to lie down to allow them to drain into the chambers until the rectum is emptied and the threads are visible; if necessary, use tweezers or your fingernail to remove them, then cauterize at their roots. If the rectum cannot expel them, apply a strong and bitter suppository to wash out what remains in the rectum, allowing it to drain clearly. When the patient presents, and the threads are severed from the rectum, the treatment is mild; you can remove them with your fingernail or tweezers, then cauterize as previously described until they are healed and prevent incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you need to administer the suturing according to this manner: take a twisted thread, and put it through an awl, then draw the thread over and pierce the awl from the other side, and turn the two heads of the thread under the awl, and so make them even; tighten the thread firmly, then tie the thread, withdraw the awl, and do thus with all others, leaving one to drain the excess blood; then place upon the foundation a moist cloth in oil of roses or cerote, place it upon the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and let him lie until he convalesce, and when they are healed, apply ointment and other care until he is sane.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of dry the wound or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times, there is a sudden drying up of bile in the intestines, and by constraint of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must reset it at the point of a spatule or your nail, which does not leave moisture; then cure it until it is dry as it should be; and if it cannot dry, you must begin the scraping more forcefully than before, until it heals and becomes scalded; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formice is a small false appearance on the body, and goes away very quickly. And sometimes one finds it cold, and feels like being dead from trembling, and it comes throughout the body, more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a needle from a goose feather, or a very strong vulture feather, and place that needle on the tremor, so that the purple circles completely surround it; then turn your hand around the entire needle so that you cover the tremor entirely, and put it perfectly, and root out the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do it with a needle of spider silk or iron according to this form, and make it thin underneath and drawing on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, for you must hold with the two fingers and press. And if you see, cauterize the tremor, as is described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the shape of the shoulder
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Any time the shoulder is dislocated, it is done with a silver, arched, molten iron, or chain; and at any time these instruments are small or large, according to those for whom they are used.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those that are used in the treatment of children and who are weak and in pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of the shoulder, whether small or large, is such that the breasts are tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it should have an opening or the breasts should be tied as you see fit, and the head should be pierced through; it should have two holes on one side and one on the other; and place the medicines inside using a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce it completely with small holes, placing one digit of space between each hole. Then insert a strong thread made from boiled linen yarn twisted ten times or so into these holes, and sew up the breasts as if they were a goat’s head; when the medicine is inside, tie it tightly with a strong thread in front of the instrument, then set it in place; this is the shape of the circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine neither be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the clyster with oil or yolk of egg, or something similar, then insert it lightly. Then, the attendants withdraw their hands together as much as it is all clear, then extract the clyster, and lift the patient's legs against the wall, and if the medicine seems to come out, so let it run forth as much as it can; and if he sleeps all night, it will be greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clysterize for a disease of bowel discharge, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as much as he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are internal or a boil, then let the clyster be as subtle as for an infant; and this is the form of the subtle clyster on which the skin is compressed.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will discuss the treatments for hands and medicines according to the fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the joints or parts where they are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the impact of a stone, and sword or knife cuts, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the joints of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or thigh, or belly, or liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and will begin with simple wounds of the head, because their chapter will come later.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a chief, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a stone blow or similar things, and the skin is entirely torn and the wound great, and you slightly doubt an abscess hot: so do it soon sanguineous of the cephalic immediately if little blood comes from the wound, and let the sainie on the contrary part of the broken.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it will not sanguineous, so let its flesh be diminished, and do not drink wine, nor eat meat; and place on the wound, if hot abscesses come, only wet cotton in rose oil, or in stipitate wine; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh to all its blood, and it has not dried by air, powder, which I will say a little later; and if the fire has dried it, place on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like a sword cut and similar ones, and the edges cannot be brought together by stretching, sew them together, as I will say for wounds of the belly, concerning stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and hangs loose, and can be held only with difficulty, bind it; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat solid meats, such as heads and cooked wheat, like eggs, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find decayed skin and it does not reach the bone, bind all the decay, apply fire, then treat it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be staunched without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, tie the artery with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is light: it is that you apply this powder which binds as though the arsenic had acted upon it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live wax three parts, and make a fine powder, and apply it to the wound, and hold it tightly in place until it dries well and joins all its blood; and then dress it well, and leave it undisturbed if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one does this with wax alone, when one does not have incense nor the dragon's blood, but lets the arsenic act upon the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the surgeon has already applied a powder to the wound while it was still fresh, he should not put this powder there; but apply some digested ointments, or pulses made from oat flour mixed with water and honey until they emit heat; then treat with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound and it is small, extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about the fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	from the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.
