If the wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, there is no other means than to let the cure proceed, and put nothing restraining on them, for it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation from those lies with the brain, which is the highest member; but use medicines over them, such as washed wax in sweet water, mixed with rose oil, and boiled flax washed in the same sweet water, and other mines according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, suture and bind it with bandages, then let the wound heal.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and infected with bowels, pierce or open them lower down; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding continues, suture and ligate it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spinal cord of the throat is cut, or the nerves, and the duct through which flesh flows is guarded, so that flesh does not enter, sew the nerve above the vocal cords but do not touch the throat, placing it according to its natural figure; then restrain it properly, and let it remain for a few days, then cure with drying ointments until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, set it; and if there are pieces of bone, remove all that you can, and leave the rest until the wound rots, and the discharge is removed; and if the wound is fresh, powder it with the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have said in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or刀伤
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a spear or sword, and the wound is deep, examine whether from the wound there are signs of immediate death: then you know that the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put in powder at the first hour nor leave it open for the blood that may coagulate and enter the heart, and kill the patient; but apply a attracting ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to drain out the moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; so there will come no spasm, nor evil tremor of the heart, nor severe pain; and when you see good disposition, then you know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure then from sores and other treatments, until he is healed; and if she cannot heal, operate, and you know that there is a fistula; treat her as we should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife incision, and it is simple, or worse, or on the back, treat what is in front; if it is large, sew it; and if it is small, dress it with powder; and if it is close to the bone and has cut pieces, let the wound heal, and remove any foreign objects if they are loose; and if they are not loose, leave the wound to drain, which will facilitate the extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, judge them as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	for the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from such a large wound, sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines are exposed, by which there is an introduction of foreign objects; and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a smaller wound is worse than a larger one, because we cannot put the intestines back in place without heat; for when the intestines swell soon upon feeling cold, they return to their original positions, and thus a medium-sized wound is better, as we warm the intestines to their proper places. And know that the rupture of the belly occurs in four ways: the two common sutures happen at the abdominal suture, and the sutures of other wounds on the body are also common; but they are more appropriate with the suture of the abdomen, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and no intestinal matter is present, and it is easy to close, this can be done by one of two methods: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in a proper manner: moisten a sponge or a cloth with warm water only, or you can boil it in water with cinnamon and cipres and spice, and wash the intestine until the swelling is removed; and once this has been done, let it cool so that it may be applied to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestine with water or with boiled and cooked mallows, for by these it becomes easier to introduce into the body a small amount; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and let the first cure be made when the cutting is finished, as there should not be much cutting unless necessary; and this is the tool for making the incision: so cut inward along the curve and do not deviate, and here is its form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine has protruded, replace it rearward according to its natural form in its proper place if you have the ability, for this requires movement.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the area below the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the area above the abdomen, you should raise his head and hips higher than the parts below, and likewise if the rupture of the abdomen is in one of the two halves, you should place things such that the severed part is higher than the other; and thus you should administer as I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And for small wounds, use what is provided to you. Then have at hand the minister of pine resin that can seal the entire rupture with its sap; and close the lips together; this is the common method of suturing, and it involves threading a needle or more, according to the width of the wound. Leave a space of about an inch from the head of the wound, and insert one needle with strong, thick thread; pierce both sides of the skin with two needles placed beneath the inner layer, making sure to pierce through that part, and bring the two ends of the siphac together in a knot. Then pass the thread twice around the needle from both sides, and close the wound by bringing the edges of the skin and siphac together appropriately. Leave a space of about an inch, and insert another needle; then follow the same procedure as with the first needle until the entire wound is closed. Use needles that are medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, because very fine needles can tear through all the flesh, and very thick ones may not enter well: thus, they should be of moderate size. Do not insert the needles too deep into the flesh and skin to avoid tearing and reopening the wound before suturing is complete; then remove the tips of the needles so that they do not irritate the patient while sleeping, and place small cloths or gauze over the needle points for easy removal, leaving them until the wound heals. This method of suturing with needles is more suitable for smaller wounds, as one needle suffices for a second suture; it involves bringing together both sides of the skin and siphac on a single needle with moderate thread. When you have pierced all four ends together, withdraw the needle to the part where you began, following the manner in which we join fabrics. Leave a space between each stitch equal to about an inch and a half; this type of suture is effective, and I once sewed a wound from a man's abdomen that was cut by a knife, measuring more than a palm in length, with intestines protruding two palms, located within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine to its place after twenty-four hours, and the wound healed in fifteen days, and I cured it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and placed clean cotton twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle, and thread it from the outside into the inside; when it has pierced through the heart straight on, leave the end of the siphon or seam where you have threaded the needle, and pierce it again from the inside out. The understanding of this stitch is that you sew as a leatherworker would sew leather, leaving the siphon once on one side and then the other, until the entire suture is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen precisely describes, is such that any person does it by assembling the two parts naturally and applying one end of the thread to the other end, in this manner: insert a needle or end of the thread near, and make a single piercing through that side, leaving the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle, and make a piercing from the outer part to the inner part, at the two ends of the thread; and this is the best method of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and anyone testifies, that one should suture the belly with two needles, or it has thread in each; and one must thrust one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds. And know that when the tear is within the belly, the suturing is more grievous than on other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, as the surgeon has drawn out, you set back the intestines, and the gut. Then put on powder to encourage flesh growth, and if the surgeon has drawn out, you put on any ointment that is present until the wound heals; and stitch the flaps, and bind the cheeks, and the groin; then treat the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you have no medicines, you put on old cotton soon as it begins to exude fluid, and change it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of other medicine in many conditions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not communicate with the principal members, it is fitting that you moisten fine linen in tempered warm oil, or in rose oil, and put it between the layers, and under the edges; and if there is pain or suppuration in boils, and often happens, use black wine enemas, especially if the suppuration comes to the intestines; and perforate from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is torn, and this is due to the problem of the veins that are there, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the head of the thighbone jumps out of the wound, reset it behind as with the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned to red or black, then you must ligate the vein that is black, to prevent blood from flowing, because there are veins and arteries there; then remove what is between the ligation, and place both heads over the part below the wound to the front for easier extraction when the thighbones fall out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the vein
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are ruptured and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some individuals, for I have seen men who were pierced by a lance, either on the right side of the stomach; the wound became walled off and turned into a fistula, through which excretions and wind passed; I treated it as best as I could, and continued to carefully tend to it until it healed, binding the edges.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it heal, I doubted whether the patient had pain in his stomach. There was no such pain, but he improved and ate and drank well. Some surgeons said that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it should be tied in this manner: take thread of large needles, then bring the edges of the wound together, and when the thread has opened the mouth, place it between the two edges so that it closes the mouth; then bind the head, and it will hold so that it cannot be untied. Then put another thread after in the same manner as before until the wound is completely closed, and leave the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief burns in the intestine, and causes no harm to the patient, one can sew the intestine with a thin thread made from the intestine of an animal: take the head of this thread of intestine that is most undehairered, then tie at the head of this thread of fine linen twisted, then put the thread on the needle, and suture the intestine, and tighten at the wound; and this method of suturing for a tremor does not differ from the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially in one of the larger intestines, there is nothing that can be known, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula or it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals, is universally called a "fistula," and especially when it is closed and round.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true nodation hard and white, where no pain is felt, and it is also very thin like a bird's feather; sometimes clear hollow, and at other times thick; sometimes small, and at other times large; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed, and there is no flesh, can only be discharged through one of the nine causes: namely, by the little amount of blood or flesh; or for its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, and above the edges, that does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the bones are rotten, and the matter has a bad quality; or the medicine used in treatment is not good; or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature; or due to the nature of the region where digestion is delayed and health is slow, and naturally swollen; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the treatments with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it must be that I shall teach you the treatment of an abscess caused by manual intervention.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that an abscess can occur in all parts of the body; for there are abscesses that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or in the liver, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or in the spinal column, or in any joint of the hands or feet; and so it affects the principal part of the limb, and similar ones.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all abscesses of this nature are a serious concern for health, and there is no cure except labor and ignorance; and if there is any abscess that does not come from the veins or arteries as I have said, and you have confidence in its treatment and can recognize it, take a thin tent of wire or iron, if the abscess is straight, hold it steady; and if the abscess is curved, use a fine, flexible tent made of plonc, because the plonc can bend around the curve. And if the abscess has openings and you cannot thoroughly examine it with tents, irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture spreads from one opening to another and cleanses it; then hold it firmly so that you can determine whether there is bone or nerve, and whether it is fully drained, and ask the patient where he feels pain when pressed, and where exactly. And when you truly know its location, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, as I have told you, then treat it according to what I have said, removing any foreign matter and decayed flesh inside; and continue the treatment until it is healed. If the abscess is deeply embedded in a straight line, you must thoroughly drain it as much as possible, then place wet tents soaked in medicinal water around it, letting them fill up to the top of the abscess, so that the medicine can erode any remaining excess from within; and afterward apply healing ointments until it is fully healed; if it does not heal through this method, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is decayed due to the abscess, then treat it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve is not damaged or the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then let the king (healing) be performed until all the corruption is removed, then cure the matters affecting flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and return to bowing as before, know that you have not yet gone far enough: so uncover and rest until you are at the core, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, that you cannot remedy it; and there is no other means but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can remove it with tongs, extract it with an appropriate instrument; and if there are many bones, remove them all, and do not leave any one. And if moisture opposes you and there is no error or fear, cut the flesh and bone, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, put something corrosive on the wound to rot it, and leave it until the flesh is rotten beneath the bone, then the bones will be lighter; and if it is a large bone, such as in the thigh or leg, reset only the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then restore the wound; and if there is much of the corrupted part, coming close to the marrow of the bone; you must excise and cauterize everything up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is set; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around XXX years of age, who had pain in his leg due to a cause within the body. The materials came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess. There was no way to drain it; but the people, out of their folly, opened it excessively so that much material drained, and it became a fistula. Many cavities appeared that continuously discharged pus and moisture from the body. For more than two years, many people treated it, and there was no wise man in the art of the hand until I was called; and I saw his leg and the medicines used to treat him, and what drained through the cavities was a large amount of pus. The body of the young man turned red, and had an amber color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one went against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened then, and cut into one of the openings enough to discover a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and pierced, with corruption extending into the bone within; I saw what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, being only what I removed; and began to restore the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not缝合；随后又开始了，再次切开骨头如前所述，发现腐败延伸至骨内，并处理了腐败部分，然后用药物恢复伤口；它迅速痊愈并缝合，不再需要重新开始这项工作，除了病人因虚弱无法忍受以及我对他的死亡恐惧。
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often there is bloodletting due to evacuation, but it was completely healed, and in the place of the bone grew a hard scar, and it was well positioned and had no harm or adverse effect at all, neither externally nor internally.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated in this manner: take a ligature, and stretch it at the end of the bone that protrudes, and order someone to extend it upwards; put another ligature of wool, larger than the first ligature, over the scar above the bone, and tie the ends so that you pull the corrupted flesh away from beneath, and uncover the flesh above the place where you wish to set it, that the bone does not bleach the flesh; and place a hot coal or a board under the bone to cook the corrupted flesh; and must continue to do so as long as corruption can be seen and felt, and do so again at another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then place a hot coal underneath, and afterward stretch from one part to the other the corruption, and let the soother be as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and the bone on the other side that contains it; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there is no old one but to copper; and if the corruption is where a knife from the hand or foot strikes, this thing is very strong, but still you must inquire about that corrosion, how it appears; and cleanse in all ways that you can, but let not the vein or nerve hinder you; know that the incisor and tendons for copping these bones are many, according to the arrangement of the bones and their appearance, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and because of this, it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each semblance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the evidence of the signs of diseases; so consider the instrument you need according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The shoulder dislocates either internally or externally; and when you have treated the corrosion with medicinal care and it does not improve, you must cut that member until you reach the place where the corrosion comes from, so that the patient escapes either death or the greater malice of the member's defect; and the signs are that the member turns black, seeming as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, the corruption of the member spreads to another member and takes over the entire body; so hasten to cut, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion, viper, and similar, and the corrosion is on the head of the arm, then cut, and do not give it time to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes just to the hand, cover at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come just to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut with the knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and there are no means of remedy except for the quantity of its virtue; and thus do when the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes in the first joint, cover after the other joint; and if it comes or pierces, cover all the pierced area; and if it rises in the leg, cover at the joint near the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means but to let the patient die; and the manner of covering or sewing the limb is that you tie over and under, extend some ministers below, and some others above, and you separate the flesh which is between the two ties as wide as a span, until the bone is revealed; then cover or sew, and place a linen bandage from each side, so that the sinew does not touch the healthy flesh, and brings another lesion and abscess to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if the flow of blood comes when you work, cautery the limb hastily, or place some restraining powders on it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, and bind the injured limb with an appropriate bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a certain man: he had a blackness that seemed like a burning fire, and this corrosion came first on his toe of his foot, so as to encompass all the foot; and when the doctors saw the corrosion, they hastened to cauterize the foot, and it healed. Soon after, the corrosion returned on his hand's thumb, and he came to me, and I placed reflective things after cleansing the body, but the corrosion did not cease; and he asked that I amputate his hand, but I would not, as I had hope of reflecting the matter; and I doubted also that if I were to cut his hand, he would die, for the virtue of man was weak; and he despaired altogether and returned to his land, and hastened to cauterize his hand, and it healed; and I do not recount this story except in case one needs another, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Sometimes an abscess occurs in the flesh, and remains so long that it gathers a great amount of pus; then it bursts and drains, and the pus leaps out, and the bones remain visible, as if they were vessels; and the skin above is as delicate as fine thread, and does not reach to the bone or to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it extends so long that it reaches the bone perfectly, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you peel away all of this skin, especially when it is delicate, as fine thread; and does not rupture for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have reason to believe that the skin will rot and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with a clyster thus: look whether the abscess is large, and the pus within has a foul smell, then prepare an Egyptian medicine in this manner: take aloe, oil, and litharge equally, and cook them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red, and becomes as thick as honey; then take of it according to your need, mix it with water and honey, and administer the clyster to the side, and hold the puncture. Leave the medicine on for two hours, then drain it out carefully; do this many times until the abscess is drained and the foulness removed; and if such medicine is not present, you can use ash water, taking vineyard ashes, pour water over them, leach it, and administer as a clyster, until you know that the side is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot bear this Egyptian medicine or the water of ashes, you can prepare a clyster with water and honey, adding some litharge; or use honey and wine mixed, where the honey has properties to cleanse and wash, and the wine causes the abscess to rupture; and when you have done this, and you believe that the side is well cleansed, administer a clyster that produces flesh in it, using plaster of Paris, mixing it with rose oil and wine; or use some medicines and ointments, about which I have said their properties, treating them accordingly; and if the opening of the abscess is small and the clyster cannot enter, you can slightly enlarge it with a metal instrument, and place on a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, you should sew it up so that only enough space remains for the clyster to enter, and if the opening where pus flows is above, you should cover it more below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the wound is perfect, do not allow flesh to fill it in; and if you cannot sew the skin as you see fit, prepare it in such a manner that the bow (thread) runs to the lowest part of the skin where it is, for when the wound is perfect, do not allow flesh to fill it in and if you cannot stitch the skin as you see fit, prepare it in such a manner: that the bow runs gently downward, and leave nothing of the thread; and take consolidative medicines to place over the healthy part, and keep them under a linen drape that covers all the healthy part; then sew with force toward the hole of the breast a bit larger than the first, for there is ointment souef on the other drape according to the size of the hole, and put it on the hole of the wound to ease the bow, and do not remove the large drape outside until after many days once; and that which is under the hole of the breast, often remove to take out the bow, and know what comes from the bow, if it be venom or little or enough, or digested or undigested; and keep watch lest the patient feel pain or numbness, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has extended in such a manner and you see the nature that comes up on the hole of the wound, know that the breasts have already swollen, and approach health; and then release the wound in the morning, or on the third day, and when you release the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast expels an undigested bowel after many days, know that the breast does not become hardened.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons cut after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds heal slowly with much effort, and of those who do the opposite; and if an undigested bowel suddenly appears from the breast after many days, know that the breast does not become hardened; and if the breast heals slowly and is distant, apply drying medicines to its substance and to its virtue, such as a diaphoretic ointment, for there is a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take a diaphoretic ointment, make it with rose oil, and infuse it with old wine equal in quantity; then heat and use it; and if such an ointment is not available, cook honey thickened, and use it when needed; and mix myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them on honey when it is on the fire, and wrap them in a cloth, place them on the breast, and sometimes administer long pepper and roots of celestial lilies, which are as fine as flour of coriander and centaurium; and use simples or compound medicines: grind them, make powder, and put it on the honey as I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged and not cured by this treatment, know that the corruption is deep and affects the bone, or hard members, or ligaments; so treat the fistula from the cure, as we said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Painarice is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or foot, or by chance arises in other toes; and when it matures and one does not take care of it, it comes to a full-blown abscess, spreading and discharging pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and by chance even the whole nail; and brings corrosion up to the bone, causing painful swelling of the finger, and the color turns foul.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the wound does not heal, then you must cut away all the remaining superfluous tissue from the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauteries are much great help if the bone is sound and the nail is whole; and if the nail presses on the flesh and begins to prick, and the blisters, then you must put a rag under the nail so as not to prick the flesh, and let it rise up, and peel that subtle and gently, and place over the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then cure with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, you must peel it and draw forth forcefully, for as long as the bone is decayed, it cannot heal; and if you see the bone decayed, you must peel it according to what was previously said, then cure it until it is healed; and if it is injured and swollen, and it feels great pain, you must first heal it; then peel the nail with a sharp spatula by cutting across, and watch that the cuts do not come up to the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too great pain; and if this happens, place something above it that will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the sore came from the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	the dislocation that arises in some men by accident is either all fleshy, and sometimes has a tear or it has bones, and once it has a nail, and none of them arise at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some knuckle.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	That which arises in any knuckle of the thumb does not move, and that which arises at the joint of the thumb may sometimes move; the size of that which is fleshy is light, in such a manner: cut it at its root with a broad blade.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which arises at the root of the joint is grievous to treat: so hold it with copper.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which is born or must be done last, it is necessary that you cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate blade, and cure it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The symptoms that come together in this way come from birth, or suddenly from a wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut this wound so that it heals according to its natural form; then place between two moist cloths or pieces of wool soaked in rose oil, to prevent them from healing too quickly; or you place between two thin pieces of linen, until the edges are properly joined.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If the wound comes together with one of these two using the palm, cut this wound as is fitting.
des vils	of the wretched
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	of the veins swollen enveloped full of excessive melancholic humours, which come from many members of the body; and more occurs in legs of those who walk and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer to him once an evacuation of black bile, and then cure him with the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The iron cure is performed in two ways: one is by cutting and draining the black blood; and the other way is to open the vein and draw all the black blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is performed in this manner: first, immerse the leg in very hot spring water until the flesh becomes tender. Then, scrape the limb of the patient from below the knee to the part just above the knee; next, make a cut in the vein at one point, or two, or three, with a wide incision. Lift and drain the black blood by hand from one end to the other, until as much blood flows as the patient can tolerate. Then close the wound and instruct the patient to rub it with meat juices rich in black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The application of the leeches is done in this manner: hold the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in a bath, and raise the leg with warm water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it on fire, and place a cloth over the vein from the ankle to the top of the knee, or below the ankle; then cut the skin at an inch, and cauterize the vein from each side until it appears when touched; and it will appear red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then place leeches under it until it rises from the skin, and then let it down to an inch, then place another cloth above three fingers; then cauterize the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with the leach as you did before, and let it down to another inch, so as you did first; then cut a different size, or more if needed, then lift it, and cut at the toe part, then draw and lift until it reaches the second size; then draw from size to size until it is all drawn out, then cut it; and if you cannot draw and lift it, place a needle with a strong double thread under it, and tie and pull, and place leeches over it, and turn your hand in one direction and another until it comes out; and beware that it does not stick, for if it sticks, you cannot draw nor lift it, and it will be harmful to the patient; and when you have drawn all of it, put wet wool soaked in wine and rose oil over the site of the wound, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must cut it crookedly, but do not clip it; and draw it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of iron with which one clips the vein is curved, and one does not cut, but only clips the vein; and it is of large curvature, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but as we have said, it should be large.
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is inserted in limbs, in warm parts where no herbs nor trees grow, and in earth where there is no moisture; and by chance it may arise elsewhere than in limbs, and this happens from putrefaction that comes from under the skin, as serpents and worms do, inserting themselves between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that there comes into the leg a very great inflammation, then change the eyes, and begin the vein to issue forth, as one root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the shoulder opens, it must be wrapped with a piece of lint about one and a half inches to two inches wide, and the wick, and let the lint hang over the leg, and every time there is no point on the outside, wrap the area again with the lint and wick; if it is too long, cut off a part of it, and wrap the remaining with it, but do not cut at its root until it is completely issued; for if you cut it, it will enter the flesh and cause an abscess, putrefaction, or swelling; because of this, it must be treated little by little until the entire length is issued; there have been cases where this vein, when treated from five inches to ten inches in length, or a man who had one issue from ten inches in length, and when you cut it, pour one drachm or puncture, and pierce it thoroughly so that all of it issues out; let the matter inside be drained, and apply anti-pus medicines for several days, then treat it as with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes from this vein many pains, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot or hand, and there comes much bruising, and where veins burst; treat it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers which arise between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often occurs in cattle, and is a small worm which arises between skin and flesh, and travels up and down throughout the body, feeling well as it goes from limb to limb, until it reaches the skin where it goes, and bursts forth; and it is engendered by putrefaction of certain humors, as come from serpents and worms and ascarides or intestines; and doubt arises about its malice, for when it travels through the body and climbs to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn, one cannot force it as it goes: therefore, you must tie the vein above and below with a strong thread tightly, then cut and draw it out. If the fluid is completely drained from the flesh, and you do not find any, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greater harm it does is that it can corrupt the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or close to the eye, hold strongly beneath it, then cut and draw it out. The patient must use cleansing of body from medicines dissolutive for bad putrefied humors, and beware of meats causing fermentation.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vакирир", and is a pain that comes into some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen those whom I say this of.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and shortly after, I saw it rise as if a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything, like living silver when it is cut from another piece; the pain departed from that place and pierced into the shoulder, and then a little while later spread throughout the body, until she came to the other arm; then she told me that it went around within the body, as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how it moved in this manner from member to member, for I had never seen this disease proceed in such a way.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Every way, I wished well to move the pain from there to another place, but I did not wish it so much as I saw in the woman; and I thought that it was because the woman had a hard core, with veins uncovered, and because these wind weaknesses were constrained; and they do not appear according to this reason to those who have soft bodies and veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to treat this illness, and the patient feels this pain, if it appears as we have said, cleanse above and below quickly, and then apply on until those wind weaknesses constrained at that place are gone; and cauterize the place. And if you do not see it with your own eyes, treat it as those that expel winds, such as bitter pills, blistering wafers of serapin, and similar things.
des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are of various kinds, according to their shapes and the places in which they lodge.
