Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of their kind is that some have large points, and small ones, and hooked ones, and fused ones; and some have two angles, and those with tongues, and those with pieces. And the one that lodges in any limb does so in various ways: or it may lodge in a principal member such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it lodges in any part of these limbs, and the signs of death, which I will tell you about later, appear: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many ways; and when none of these bad signs appear, and the arrow is not fully extracted, you should remove it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and a vein that is above the brain bursts, is when there is scotomia and sodor and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps it comes from the nostrils or the ears; and perhaps it affects speech and voice; and a moist white discharge from the wound as if it were pus, and it appears like boiled flesh; and if you see this sign, keep to treatment, and extract the arrow if it is there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it strikes or pierces the heart is that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were embedded in something hard, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like a pulse, and brings dark blood, and causes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never came out is that without bubbles of foam it jumps from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and sighs loudly and refreshes himself with cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls into the cover of the foot, it affects the small bones; it causes great pain and sighing; and all the limbs from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls onto the stomach, by chance it jumps from the wound with some undigested meat.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls onto the belly, and it jumps out leaving some hay through the intestinal tract, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine spurts out and flows, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, such as the arm, neck, throat, shoulder, auxiliary bone, spine of the back, femur, and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you would do otherwise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck or pierced in the root of the nose: I tried it, and extracted it from the other side under the ear fat, and he recovered without any difficulty.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And draw out an arrow that fell into the grease of the eye beneath the paper, and the arrow was lodged, and one could not reach it from the side of the wood, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish bow, light as iron without ears; the patient recovered, and no bad accidents befell him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And drew out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arab with ears: I plucked the barbs, and drew it out thoroughly, and the Christian recovered.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And drew out an arrow from the man, which had pierced his side or belly, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, he did not change his condition at all. I cut into the arrow, removed it, and drew it out thoroughly, and he had no bad accidents.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to treat a man who has an arrow that fell or pierced his back, and the wound was sewn up; and the arrow remained inside, and did not change its natural position, nor caused any harm in any of its natural functions.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you wish to treat another man, who has an arrow in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and he remained thus suffering great pain; and many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And an arrow struck a man among the king's princes, which it had hit in the neck, and was slightly倾斜向右侧；并且那支箭完全穿透了。我被叫去为它治疗，在它落下的三天后。
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with great subtlety, and did not feel it; and there was a puncture and pain beside his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I applied a poultice of atrative and digestible plaster on it, because the eyes were not swelling; and I found the eye affected by the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and redressed the wound again. The patient remained in this state for a long time, until he felt the arrow in his nose on the following day; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicinal substance to the wound for several days until it was opened, and examined it; I felt the tip of the arrow which was corroding at the site; then I continued applying that corrosive medicine in the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow became clearly visible; and it passed through well, taking more than four months. Then I widened the wound so thoroughly that I could use pliers to extract it from both sides, but it would not come out; therefore, I continued examining and devising methods with various instruments until I successfully extracted it using properly made pliers, as described in the form shown at the end of this chapter.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeon judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and the wound was sewn, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or have I told you about the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you apply your cure to what I do not say, for books cannot take in everything; but wise masters compare on very little, and on what is present and lacking, find new work, and nine instruments, for the descent of foreign things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are of two kinds according to where they enter: either by the place where they enter or by another part; and that which enters through the place where it enters is an arrow entering the flesh, and does not enter again now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not burst now, let it be left until the flesh rots entirely, and the pus is released; and also if it is embedded in the bone and cannot come out, leave it so for some days, and change it each day; then it will burst, and if it does not burst, pierce through to all the innermost parts with something subtle, until the flesh inside is widened, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is embedded in the bone of the head and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and any of the symptoms I have said to the patient: do not draw it out at all, but let it be until it is equalized after a few days, for if the arrow comes just to the syrinx, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not pierced deep only into the bone, and does not come as far as the surface, and the patient remains without any bad accidents for several days, then the device for extraction should be used.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be removed easily, I administer taretors into it, as I have said; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is embedded in the body and one cannot see it, keep quiet about it entirely. And if you feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is neither bone nor nerve nor vein, cut open the skin so that the wound becomes larger; then extract the arrow if possible, and if it has parts attached such as feathers that hold it, remove the flesh that is embedded on both sides up to where you can reach. Then break or bend the feathers of the arrow until you can extract it; and be very careful not to break the arrow, as this would make extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, let it remain until the joint is rotten, then remove it, for the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding contraries you, apply what we have said regarding treatment in this chapter; and be careful of incising the nerve or vein, and find a way to extract the arrow gently so that it can be done quickly or slowly, firmly or carefully; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell upon him, for this is the greatest help that can be given, and if you cannot do this, place him as the signs indicate.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another direction, or if it penetrates something else, or if the skin is swollen in such a way that one can see or feel it: cut there, as deep as the forceps can grasp, and then extract it: if it is now embedded.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand round, until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then restart the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is still in, push the whole shaft; and if the shaft falls out, when you see that a thrust is needed, I will administer the instrument thrusting, so that the point of the arrow enters the hole of the instrument; and then push with force, and if the arrow is lodged, I will push the instrument at the point entering in, to facilitate the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touching, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as needed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls or pierces in the belly or bladder or side, and it is near, you may try to extract it; and guard against extracting the vein or the nerve, then extract it, and suture the wound if need be; and treat until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the feathered rod is similar to the feather of a bird, to push at the tip of the arrow, as shown in the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for pressing and knowing this is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins of the body common
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	of veins from which one is healed there are thirty-one, of which sixteen are principal, that is to say: two jugulars which are behind the ears, called "herbech" in pairs; and the two arteries which are in the temples visible; and the veins which are in the lacrimal glands of the eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein which runs through the forehead; and the vein which is on the nose; and the two subclavian veins which are at the neck; and the two veins which are in the upper lips above the mouth, these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the veins which are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly bleeds are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and they call it "vein of the head"; and the median is called "fascia," and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and they call it "vein of the belly," and it is above the flexor, and it is that from which one bleeds, which clearly appears above the pocket.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the basilic vein is the vein that is between the auricular and annular, and it has two tendons; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one of which is below the corona of the pocket on the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein called "nephros," which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The treatment of veins located behind the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of this treatment, as I have said, are that you reset the patient's head, and rub the area or veins with a rough cloth. Then bind the patient's neck to a screw so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two holes depending on the head: hold them with your thumb, and where you feel the pulse under your thumb, prick; then take the lancette, insert it beneath the vein up to the bone, lift your hand all along the vein upwards, cut and remove the skin and vein well twice through, and let the blood flow out until you see it. Then drain and bind it so that it heals; and I have already spoken of the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples, it is worth old numbness, stiff, and accustomed to blindness, and in the body of tears on their eyes; and the quality of this health is as I say: and it is that the patient restrains his throat, so that the two veins clearly appear; and one feels a pulse under your thumb, and then begins to cut; then lift the heart over the vein up to your index finger, and place the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and the cap, as you have done with the other veins, and draw off the blood according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then form it well, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of them regarding their tying and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The sainie of the vein on the forehead is as effective as the cephalic in ancient headaches and migraines, and for redness; and its quality is that the patient feels pain along the path of the vein when it is compressed; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is as follows:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the point on the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity you see; then release the pain in the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is sound, and do not repeat the work with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	In all cases, it is not appropriate for the flames to be too hot; and apply the heat from the side, as the bone is nearby, and by chance, the flame may break the bone when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the two eyelids helps with the eyes, and for headache, and for flushing, and for the redness in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the qualities of their health are such that the patient draws his soul out through his neck by twisting any one vein, as before; then the savior, and let the saving pass through a little bit long like a flame a little bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is subtle, by chance it breaks; then make the blood flow as much as you need, and then tie with cotton, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The health of the vein of the neck is good for water and strong poisoning, and for face diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the qualities of its health are such that the patient draws his soul out by twisting the vein, then pulls his neck towards your left hand, and takes a subtle long flame, and sticks it between the lip in the space which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well without, and the breath will begin to flow now; and do not go too perfect, and make the blood flow as much as you need according to your necessity, then tie it for a night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The sinews of the two glands help in narrowing the throat, and in the beginning of a mixture, and much disease, and empitying, and corrosion, and herpes, and estiomenes; and the quality of the sinew is that the patient draws his neck away from one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be above the patient's head, and the patient lie on the seat, then make a cut along the long vein somewhat widely, then draw temperate blood, or as much as is needed; then do another thing in the other vein, then untie the thread, and compress the veins moderately, that the patient does not choke; and let him remain until morning, so that the wound may heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of the sinew of the glands
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The veins of the lips above help in swelling in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of lips, and around the nose and between them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the qualities of the vein are such that it makes the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and they can be known by their blackness, and by the small black veins around them: cut both of them, and if you do not know them, and are in doubt, cut the largest from each side, and similarly make cuts above and below, for it is done in the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the disease beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The disease of the veins that are beneath the tongue helps after the disease of the cephalic vein, and it is in the narrowing of the throat, and diseases of the uvea, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the venous remedy is such that the patient's disease becomes clear before your eyes in the sunlight, and it eases the tongue, and you look beneath on each side a black vein: therefore one is healthy and the other also, and do not apply too much, for beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the throat that are commonly treated can be cured in two ways: either by pricking with a sharp martyr flame or with a subtle olive oil as you hear cut, and it is called "anisil"; and they are large and subtle according to the size and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the martyr's flame is very renowned, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it has necessity to open veins full of thick blood and containing much blood and turbidity; and this is the form of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more pointed subtle, and is for cleansing thin veins, or where there is thin yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The cleansing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are in the throat, neck, side, and abdomen; and it is suitable for the physician to bleed by incision and to avoid the artery beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery, and bleeding comes forth, it must be stemmed, as I have said; and fire should not be applied, but clamped like a pincers.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open clearly, it must be extracted, and replaced with another; or if you wish to use any vein in its place for the incision through the arm: it will open clearly; and clamp it with a pincers of flax, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the site of the incision, it must be thus that you extract the arm, touching the site until you feel the pulse; then mark the site with a pencil, and then bind the arm, clamp the vein with a flax pincers; and beware that you do not pierce the artery when you see the site swollen, for this is the artery: avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see bulging upwards as with urine in a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that it is blood from an artery: then hasten, and place your finger longwise, then remove your finger when the veins have stopped; several times this happens; if the limb is wounded, leave it thus, and do not move the patient in fear; let them remain still until they are healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the veins are not stopped, and it pains you, and medical help is not present, cut the artery if it appears, for the head of the blade will stop it; stop the veins.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a bark of willow, split it, and take one half and bind it well just to the other day; if the veins stop, that is good; if not, treat it as we have said, using powders that stop blood; but the bindings are not griés for many positions due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The vein of the arm for drawing blood above the shoulder and below the body helps to treat blood from the head, as it is composed of the basilica and cephalic, as we have said; it is necessary for the patient to guard against the nerve beneath, and if he points too deeply, and finds the nerve, and it swells, and the health is harmed, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in any man due to its subtlety, it is necessary that you anesthetize the vein with the instrument; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it open along its length.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The cephalic vein helps, as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; it is necessary to anesthetize by pricking with olive oil flame or myrtle oil, for this is the safest of all veins, as it has no nerve or artery beneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In every way, it is necessary to seek the lightest touch, and do not overdo it if needed for the first time, and one recommences; and by chance swelling occurs in some people after the first attempt, but it does not cause any harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the sinew is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about sinew is that sinews are not strained except to maintain health and avoid future diseases; and the sinews should be treated in one of the three veins: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and one should treat the sinews at the beginning of prayers on bended knees, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of fullness appear; and one should treat the sinew on the first or third day after two or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The remedy given for diseases has no fixed hour appointed, but when need is of day or night, at all hours and in every season; and it is not fitting to treat children under fourteen years, nor women with child from the fourth month until seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Old people who have passed sixty years should not be treated either.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when any wish to be treated, whether in the morning or evening, it is fitting that they cleanse their intestines with a light enema, if they have not retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw from the intestines their putrid superfluities harmful to the principal limbs; nor should those who are too salty from meat, drunk to excess, or dropsical be treated. And when one desires to treat after colic pain, vomiting, and evacuation of the bowels, frequent copulation and travail, staying awake and fasting, and those whose virtues are diminished by weapon or body; then subtlely let the humors, if they are gross, through meat and drink and medicines, if you have the power. Then between bathing, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and treat the vein below the third toe, as we have said; and on that day avoid work, labor, and lustful acts, and similar things; remain bound and laid down, and let the one treating be higher than he whom they are treating, and rub their arm two or three times, then gently extract the ligature above. For when it is too tight or loose, it cannot correctly draw the blood; then rub the leg with your hands until the veins swell, and you feel them; afterwards anoint the treturer’s hand with a little old oil, then place his left hand under the vein near where they wish to treat, ensuring the vein does not become bruised by the iron.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as cords in the physician, and some are full of windiness, such that when one applies fire to them, they recoil from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus are of this kind; and if he opens the vein, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the physicians must be cautious about these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; but if not, one should attempt to open it again slightly below or above that place, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is swollen, and the patient feels pain, one should leave it for a day or two, and not bind the arm: perhaps abscesses will form. Do not go into a bath, but continue with the operation if the physician wishes; and if the opening is small, or the vein thin, and you doubt whether there is as much blood as you see, then apply the flame directly to that opening; work quickly, while the limb is swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb swollen, do not begin healing until it is healthy, and put a little olive oil over it, for it lightens the body of blood, and causes the oil to dry up that which is in this place; thus administer the oil juice in each wound that you heal the veins, to staunch the course of blood; and the same thing is done with treacle and bowe of haws when one puts them over the limb; so subtlely does it penetrate and separate when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes an abscess large, which often happens, even when it is not healed more than that one time or the opening of the vein is small, then hasten, and put over the limb a sponge moistened in water and salt a bit warm, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood from the vein has issued. And if it remains on the limb after some days any blackness or greenish color, it does not harm it at all; and if you see, put over it any preparation of aloes or myrrh immersed in calamus, mustard, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often an abscess and appearance on the skin of the basilica: therefore place your hand there, and if you find the area soft under the pressure of the hand, that is the bad appearance.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply anything of what we have said, for by chance it might cut the artery; but make him a dry plaster to harden the area, and then treat with other remedies until he is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it becomes red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is fitting for him who is full and strong, and has need of blood extraction, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for him who is weak, do the opposite, and he should be healed little but often, and you must heal in cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of healing is saved from running of blood and compression of nerve, and it is better than long or wide wounds.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for him whose body requires nourishment during healing, it is fitting to give moist food in juice of pomegranates; if he is heated, draw blood three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, eat moist food before healing in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and well-odored syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it swells on the side, after the discharge of much blood, it must inhale broth of flesh, and fragrant subtle syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if it sees fit to let the arm swell and be injured again, when it is weakened by great swelling, it must be allowed to swell little by little, according to the quantity of its virtue continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever sees fit to let the arm swell after the first swelling, and if it has strong virtue, it must be allowed to swell for seven hours after the first swelling, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one sees fit to be injured on another side, it must be injured on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood within the body which is already heated, and it brings fever; so it is necessary to draw out great quantity, and widen the opening until it heals in the flesh; then when you fulfill all conditions of health, and place your hand on your pulse where it is healthy, that death not come from under the flesh; and this happens often, when physicians are negligent; but it is not proper when you see release the arm, and let blood a second time, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly upon it; nor if it is crooked, that you stretch the arm quickly, for that would be bad; but let it be until it heals a second time; or you prick at the tip of the flame, until the one who is frozen reaches from under the vein to the opening, and put some salt in water, and press lightly upon it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be, and do not compress it, until the abscess is relieved.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if the need arises to treat the blood a second time, let it be done in that very vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is treated in place of the vein in the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of treating it is that the patient puts their hand in warm water until the fingers are red; then tie it moderately so that the vein is clearly visible, and now siphon the blood from the side, not from the length or width; make the puncture large, and place the siphoning close to the joint of the hand. If no more blood can come out, put the hand back in warm water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; if it is in winter, do not repeatedly dip the hand in warm water, as it should be used more in summer than in winter; and the treatment of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve that can be damaged.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The sickness of the salvation of the right hand is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is the manner: extract the hand, and put it in hot water until the veins are swollen, if one can see them; and if the wound is crooked, and if you cover it completely, do not grieve anything; and do not go too perfectly done, because the nerve is under all stripped of flesh, and then put the hand in hot water again if the wound is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let the blood as much as it needs, put a cloth with oil and salt on the vein to seal it quickly, and do this for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sickness in the left hand is good for the disease of the mouse [likely referring to an abscess or similar condition], and do everything as I have told you for the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The soul's health is good for all diseases that are below the body, such as liver diseases, retention of flowers, disease of the reins, and of the old thighs and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its health is that diseases cause pain in hot water, and are rubbed on the vein until it pains, and tied above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot goes much urine; therefore, keep it healthy or wider vein, or at the ankle, which moves well.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the foot, watch the nerves that are beneath, and keep them healthy as well by cutting carefully; let the flaxen thread be ready.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the stone cannot come out, put the foot in water, and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the stone is needed for the first time, begin again the second time above a little, because the loins are salted; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and so do with the sponge of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The loins of the sciatic vein are at the ankle, and its stone is worth for pain in the hip when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its stone is such that the patient should enter the bath, and extract four doigts above the ankle by twisting, otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, you can stone it in all ways that you can, and by crossing it; it is better to cop it because the loins are sound, and it is very responsive to human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, search any vein from the front or back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and draw off as much blood as you see, then release the bandage, and put on a cloth and bind it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	with suction cups
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Suction cups are made of horns, or iron, or glass; and suction is performed in two ways: either by pricking and drawing blood, or without pricking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this suction without pricking is performed in two ways: either by fire or without fire; and the suction made by pricking and extracting blood is done at fourteen places on the body, of which one is right under the head; another is behind the neck; two are on each side of the neck; one is below the chin; one is on each shoulder; one is above the armpits; one is on each arm; one is on each leg; one is on each ankle; and suction does not draw blood, but only small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and for this reason it does not weaken much, as we do with a vein from a vein. And it should not be administered by fire or without fire in any disease coming from overfullness, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness it is fitting to bleed, or for custom, we shall administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or in the end, and between and in every time; for there are such as, when they have need to bleed, have a heavy head; and there are such as find fullness and redness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness before their eyes; and such as find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swelled tongue, and spit blood.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is between the months, we command them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The sinew of the muscle aids in the breaking of the head's chief... that comes to them, and it should not be after the evacuation of all the body; and this ventilation is in place of the sinew of the cephalic, and it should not be used by those of cold complexion or who have chatharre, for it does them much harm; because of this, it should not be used by those who watch nor by those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who frequently draw blood thus become forgetful, and because of this, it is necessary to place the cupping device a little more downward due to the fear of forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation at the neck is in place of the sinew of the head and the basilica vein, and because of this, it is useful for narrowing the pulse, and for cutting into the channel of the subclavian artery, and for swelling; and it should be applied only briefly, for if it holds too firmly, it can cause forgetfulness or stomach and heart issues.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The wind-vasations near the second ribs of the neck are for headaches, eyesight issues, migraines, stranglements, and tooth root pain; they are in the place of the health of the basilica. You must instruct the healer to extend his hand when placing it, not pressing the artery, and preventing any loss of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wind-vasations below the chin are for mouth diseases, gum corruption, and similar ailments that affect the mouth; they are in the place of the health of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind-vasations of the shoulders are for diseases that come from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind-vasations near the ribs are as effective as those of the third veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; you must instruct the healer not to pierce too deep, as the muscles are bare of flesh and one can feel the nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup placed on the rump is good for hemorrhoids from the fundament and below, and it should be large, made of iron, which needs to be well-treated; and by chance, if it were fine, it would break; and I make large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs cleanse openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are good for old pains in the thighs, the hips, and the bladder, and diminish tumors; and they are placed at the two ankles and the two calves, and in any case, they weaken the body after long use, and bring about paralysis in many conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the suction cup is as follows: you should first empty it and gently warm it up, then quickly place it, move it evenly, and do not stop until you see the area turn red and swell, and the reddish blood appears; then remove it, and put the suction cups back. Be mindful of the condition of the body, for some have thick flesh and clear pores: in such cases, you should pierce only once, make large wounds, and slightly deeper ones.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the vein is large, it must be pricked twice: the first time to dilate the path of the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the vein is very full, it must be pricked three times; and when we wish to draw blood little by little, we puncture only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw much blood, we begin often; and if the vein is full, pierce it thoroughly, and let the openings be such that the cords are cut suddenly, and for those who have thick skin and are hard, and have narrow pores, you should apply to the eyes of the cups anointing and dissolving oil: if it is in heat, with olive oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in cold, with mustard oil, or linden oil, or chamomile oil, or other similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluity is large and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balsamite oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being cured has flesh and large pores, it is not necessary to put any oil on it, but it should be washed after fomentation with rose water, or cold water, or mullein water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have much moisture, let them rise from almond, or mulberry water, or sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities rise from old wine, or decoction of syrup, or infusion of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and it is not advisable to cure with suction before the bath or after bathing, but one hour or two after the bath; and do not sleep after fomentation, and must be warmed when it is necessary to suction and when he is being suctioned.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch over him who is healing if he is choleric, and if the blood is too acrid and inflamed; it is fitting that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in vinegar, and similar things; and eat maggots, and meat from a dormouse, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And he who has a cold complexion, let him take syrop of honey, and medium-smelling wine between old and new, and eat little, and eat maggots and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he will be cupped, he should drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some men treacle or mace before or after cupping to comfort the principal members; and let his blood be subtle, but it is not fitting that those who are hot drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are placed without piercing are those placed on the liver, and on the lungs, and gout, and on the belly and mouth and veins and thigh, for these parts do not tolerate being pierced at their roots, and one uses fire only to draw blood from member to member, as we place them on nipples when a child nurses; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and mouth to alleviate the swelling of the member; and to relieve pain, when there is a boil or stone, it may by its attractive virtue remove the boil or dislodge the stone from its place; thus does it do when placed on the liver and lungs when there is retained windiness, and these suction cups are administered empty only to suck out; sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in diseases of the pleura, and in such a manner we fill the cup with hot water or boiled herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the suction cup applied with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two inches wide and half a palm of copper, and have or cut a small hole in the middle for inserting an needle, as for sticking a needle, and let it be of tin, with a wick in front so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb; and have in the middle a cross rod of tin or iron to put a candle holder on, and let there be both large and small ones according to the diseases and the strength of those who use them; for children's suction cups are different from adults', and thin people's from fat people's.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one must place the suction cup on the limb in this manner: take the candlewick of wax or linament, and put it into the suction cup through the cross rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup and does not burn the patient; then put it on the limb, and let your two fingers be over the hole as we have said, so that when you want to, the vapor goes out, and remove the suction cup; and around the hole, apply linament as before, and repeat often if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping applied for diseases of the lungs, for all acute conditions, there is neither a vein nor a hole, and it is not applied forcefully unless it is full of fluid, and is placed on the limb only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.
