Cupping is not applied forcefully on parts where cups cannot be placed due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; and on bare skin, such as elbows or knees, and others like them; and the quality of the cupping should be that when you find blisters in clear, sweet water without corruption, take them; and place one nut in clear water until they are familiar and have nothing inside; then bleed by incision and cupping, then rub the limb until it is red, and place the blisters on it; and when they are full and fall out, if it is a place where a cup can be placed, put it there, for this is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not so, lift the arm from the armpit, and then with water, very well, and then press it. And if the limb heals too soon after the body of the veins, make a soft linen cloth in cold water, and place it on, until the flesh be infected; and if the wounds multiply, place on vitriol broken or garlic, and similar things, until they be infected; or you put over the limb half of peeled beans, and let them be until they dry out on the limb, and will stop bleeding now. And if you have more need of it, take other veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not wish to take, rub the limb with fresh blood, or stick a needle in them until the wounds bleed, and then place them on. As soon as they smell the blood, they will dry out; and when you see that they are weeping, sprinkle a little aloes and ground salt or ashes over them, and they will heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear friend, that the knowledge contained in this chapter was not found in any of the ancient books or letters they read; and for this reason, the science has been lost in our land, for I have never found a good one among them. And I know nothing of it except through the science of ancient books, in which I studied so much that I treated of the science, and through experience, and by custom from my life. And I have here described to you what is contained, abbreviated at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters before these.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say in the prologue of this book the summary of our words and the chapters where the wise ones place their understanding, remaining on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twists or sprain comes to any person, it must be treated by healing the patient from both sides, if nothing else affects him, such as bodily weakness, or illness, or age; or if his hand is not very warm, or too cold; and he should consume cold wood, that is to say, cold javelina tusks, and meat of bird and chervil, and should not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and should not fill himself too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of a hot abscess or spread of matter in the limb; then the patient returns to his former regimen as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to feed the patient meat that promotes rapid healing or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, peas, and fish, fresh eggs, and good wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	And in the case of meat, it represents nourishment and more quickly heals the fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones in the elderly and decrepit cannot heal or set well according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not worry, reset the broken bone with large bandages which will firm up and join the limb together, until it strengthens as it was before; yet do not fully complete their work, and for this reason, they must be fed large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	And know that the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or the leg, and I will tell you all kinds of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	And there are fractures that go lengthwise, and others that go across, just like the cuts of a pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is fracture with wound, and fracture with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each kind, it has its own tool and instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings to its place; and fractures of the bone are known by the distortion of the limb, and clearly by tapping and pressing with the hand. And when there is no distortion, nor a sound upon pressing, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there may not be a fracture; but it can still have distortion, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it does not suit you to move it by hand, then apply medicines that come after this, and then hold it delicately now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that goes into the bone, and are the two parts disjoined, you must now put them in alignment equally, as abscesses covered come to life; and if abscesses hard come to life, you let them any day, until the abscesses be calmed; then put it equal to the place where you can gently and safely, and know that the restoration of the former is lighter than the restoration of that which has pieces; then hold it as it suits after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, you must set them from both sides, whether it is a hand or foot, or by your own hand for smaller members, or by two strings, or one string and your own hand; and place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you reset all additions within their places at the joint where you can, and guard that through your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and adjust well the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if it seems not quite right: straighten it beautifully, and do not hold it too tightly, nor press it as those who bring on a hot abscess and contraction to the limb through their work, as we have often desired.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in proper condition, well rest the patient so that he does not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor when turning over, nor in any other way; and be sure that the limb is securely placed so that no pain is felt.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet in proper condition, and it must be placed in such a way that no pain is felt; and take care that it is properly aligned so that no deformity occurs when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are as I have said.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are varied in smallness and in largeness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For small limbs, such as arms and thighs: it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloths; and for large ones, such as the thigh and leg: they should be wrapped with a wide and hard bandage, because the wide bandages encircle the entire large limb evenly, so that there are no wrinkles; then tie them tightly around three or four times according to the limb, and slightly tighten your hand on each bandage, then go above the break and tighten it less, so that the break can be moved a little away from the break; and soften the bandage gradually, until you see a large part of the healthy tissue, then take the other bandage, and rewrap again over the broken area; then return to the part below the break, and wrap moderately, neither too tightly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first lesson above; then place linen or cloth strips evenly between the tied bandages, so that they are all equal, then tie everything with a bandage from above, and then put on your well-made pillows if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, apply something soothing and heating for the abscess, and that reduces swelling, and leave it on for a few days; then extract with your linen strips, which should be half as wide as a thick rope, or from wood used for ax handles, or from palm ribs, and they should be of this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it must be that the linen strips which one places on the break are slightly wider and longer than the others; and should be as long as is fitting for the member's size or greatness. Then hold the linen strips in place just as you did at the first application, then tie a suitable thread over them as you did at the first application to the break; the threads must be closer together beneath, thus less so above; and it must be that the thread be medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax. For if the thread is thick, like those used by the craftsmen who make their applications from twisted linen cords, this is a great error, for the application cannot be even if it is too delicate, and it does not suit that there be less than two fingers' width between each strip.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the shoulders of the needles after the tightening in their sound places, put over them lint or a cloth bandage so that it does not swell.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	And when the wound is burned and the sinews are broken, I will describe the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not advisable to tightly bind the needles for all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not advisable to tightly bind them with needles immediately but rather after 5 days or 7, or more according to your judgment following a hot abscess occurring; and here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that sticks to the mill walls, mix it with abundant egg, and apply this mixture not too thin nor too thick. And use it, as this is the common method for applying a restorative plaster for treating many conditions, especially in women and small children, because it is neither too harsh nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster to restore fracture and dislocation and torsion: take 3 parts of bay leaves and garlic and onions and gum arabic and myrrh and musk, mix 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, mix 5 parts; saltpeter 9 parts; make into a powder, mix with honey from one egg; if the person's complexion is warm, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for torsion: take myrrh and benzoin, mix 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, mix 9 parts; camphor 6 parts; armenian wax 10 parts, grind well, compound with water or honey from one egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another plaster for joints and bones broken from their places, and relieves the pain that comes, and the cutting of the bone, and the breaking: take new wool, and the marrow in swine's fat and cooked oil, and put on the wound.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for alleviating hot abscesses, and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster to heal broken bones: take dried fig leaves, and ground ivy leaves, and grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the swelling of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of visvalve, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of cloves, of each one part; and grind them, and mix with wine, and if the members are heated, mix with moist coriander water or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply a plaster stronger than the first, when an abscess is hard and comes during the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of visvalve, and seeds of flax, balsam, hyssop, and sage, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of each one part; and grind them, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	And Hippocrates states in his book that one should not apply anything on a broken limb to restore strength that cerote made of wax and oil does, and nothing else more, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to suggest that one should apply on the broken limb things dry and a little warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another plaster useful for injury and pain: take mithridate and hemp seeds decorticated, or bird feathers, and vismale, and equal parts salt, and grind them, and make a plaster with them.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then remove it after some time, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if it is not necessary to remove it by hand. And if pain comes to the area, or itching, with no relief or swelling, you should remove it quickly, and take off the plaster now; and use a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and soak it in water, and lift the limb until the itching ceases and the pain is eased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then place on dry wool soaked in water or rose oil, and bind it tightly until you are sure of the warm abscess; and reduce inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then resume the delicate ligature, and a little plaster, but do not tie it so tight as before; and continue with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is empty and redness and pain and swelling have been removed from all parts, and you need to apply a plaster and bandage, then proceed with it as you did at first equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if none of what we have said comes to the member, and it is not dislocated after three or four or five or seven days; and at one time you leave it twenty days, according to what one sees, until the broken ends harden, and bring the alignment close to the flesh above; then restrain it more than before, and let it grow its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that the place is drying more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come; wash the dislocation with hot water each time you dislocate it, and let it be every third day, and lessen the swelling a bit; by this work then cut the nourishment from the member, and mend quickly what the foolish menders do, which leave the member deformed: this is bad, and such are fearful works, and I see nothing else but to leave it and operate properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of breaking are, and various forms, and the causes are destined; for there are breaks made by the percussion of a sword, and the neck bones break all the bone just beneath the bone, as done by a hammer or stick; and because of this, this way of breaking is called "hatchet wound.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing, and this way of breaking is called "absolute"; it includes wounds from these two breaks, whether large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a compression break, or a fracture of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar ones.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break nearby, which approaches just to the tissue beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as subtly as hairs, and is a small split, and for this it is called a "capillary" break; and if the wound made by striking with a stone, or falling, or some similar thing, causes a piece of bone to enter from below, and the edges are like those a smith makes when striking on cauldrons; so the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have or are children with moist bones, such as a child's bone; and it happens in all these types of break where small pieces come loose like splinters; and I will speak of this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And know all manners of breaks through their subtraction, and by inquiry with tests, and through the corrupt flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known in this way: when the bone is discovered and rubbed over it, black breaks appear.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take heed of the bad symptoms in the patient, and if you see any ill symptoms such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, fainting, convulsions, fever, and the eyes turning outward and becoming red, and other similar things due to various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any terrifying symptoms, and you hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the fractures come first to you, and it is in winter, then you must extract the bone before the fourteenth day after the month.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you must hasten to extract the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh beneath the bone deteriorates, and the accidents as we have said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you must split the fractured part in such a way: and you must take hold of the edge of the injured patient, uncover above the bone in all the ways you can, and more over the figure of the wound. And if bleeding from the bone occurs upon uncovering the bone, or an abscess forms, then aid as necessary, and it is that you fill the space with moistened cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses subside, and you are assured of no further bleeding; then begin to extract around the bone, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut narrowly before, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then one cuts a larger incision than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several different incisions, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron filings; and work lightly, so as not to burn the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, you must pierce it through, so that you make incisions with points, not fully through but beyond the bone at the back, and should have a margin or circle above the point, such that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each comes to its place according to the thickness of the bone, and you should have points for all parts; and this is the form of three kinds of points.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the broken bone are that you place the needle on the bone, turn to your two sides until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the needle a little further elsewhere, and do this throughout, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone which is between the parts, and do this more subtly than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you bring the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as forceps, pinchers; and beware that you do not touch the brain nor the sphenoid.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you release the tension which has remained between the bone and any other similar instrument to an incisor, but it must be more tense and finer than another incisor; and if there remains nothing of the small bones or any scales, remove them gently with instruments; then treat the wound with cloths and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galien said, which is safer; and it is very strong, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture opens up, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place beneath the head of this lancet-shaped instrument the one described here in detail.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and let the fracture be in two parts, so that the cutting is opposite the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you gently break the bone all around, and take great care of the membrane beneath; if it is dry against the bone, break the bone gently, for it can be broken very harmfully and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is cut only on top, and there are small pieces, then it must be treated by smoothing out that roughness, and removing scales with a fine razor of which you should have various quantities, to apply in each place what is most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you need to use large razors first and then finer ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other small incisions and fine fractures, you must apply it according to its direction; and this is something that is not given to him who has devoted his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the syphacia is uncovered, you must take linen cloth according to the size of the wound, and grease it with rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled two or three times, and grease it with wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; do this as lightly as you can so that you do not burden the syphacia, then apply a bandage over the other one, and do not tie it too tightly that it hurts the wound; leave it thus for one or two days, until the abscesses are calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, fennel flour, incense powder, and aromatics, and similar things; make a powder of these things and apply it to the wound, and continue administering medicaments without causing irritation; ensure that the wound is clean, do not leave the ointment or allow it to accumulate on the head cloth, for when wine accumulates on the covering of the brain, it runs down and causes great harm to the patient; because when anything sharp is applied to the syphacia, the nerves are affected above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care, if no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, there is doubt concerning it.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if night or some other evil comes only because of the medicine we have put on, that it has virtue, you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and one part of gum, and put it on the sore; then cure it in the manner of cures that it should be healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the neck above are broken, or one alone, for these are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break nor cause pain by bending or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, it must be that you set your little finger or thumb from birth, and place the break evenly within your index finger, and the pouch by division, so that the nose regains its natural figure; do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is above the nose and the fingers cannot reach the place, it must be that you set them evenly on the head of a needle somewhat large.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do the same on the other side, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses have subsided, then place tenters of linen thread on the head of the nose if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you place it on the other side, where the break is; let the wicks be so large that they fill the pores of the navel.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And any restorer should melt the wicks in butter and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It does not seem right to me, but they should be melted in a mixture of egg white and flour powder; then leave the wick until the bone is firm and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes place goose quills in its place of wicks, and insert them into the navel, and keep the wound closed, and blow with the patient facing whichever direction you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses break during the work, apply a poultice or moist cotton in rose oil, or with a little balsam.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not break during the work, apply an ointment externally, made from silkweed flour and incense powder, cooked with egg yolk. Then place light stops over it, but do not bind the nose; and if the nasal fracture is small, and broken into small pieces, extract it with suitable instruments, then stitch the wound and treat the soft tissue injuries and wounds with appropriate ointments and poultices; and if there are no internal nasal wounds, treat with splints until healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is ruptured but there is no wound open, and the break is only fissured, not broken into pieces like beams inside, one can recognize it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	When the break is in the right part of the jaw, you should place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the break is in the left mandible, you should use your right hand to gently press on the break and fix it with the other hand through an opening.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the jaw is separated into two parts, you should apply an extension to both parts, making them equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs, or rupture, strain them with a gold or silver or silk thread, then place on the broken jaw a compress, and put over it a double bandage; and place over the bandage a large well-made pad, or a piece of leather equal in size to the jaw, and fasten it at the mouth as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, release it on the third day, and then set what has changed back in place; and apply a poultice with powder from the mill mixed with abundant egg or sinew flour after you have removed the compress; and place light wool over the poultice, and if the poultice dries out and the patient's condition does not change, leave it until he is healed; many times it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a gangrenous abscess comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, reward no fragment of the bone that is removed; so subtle to remove with instruments convenient for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, enlarge it with flambes according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these fragments, and there remains none, close the wound if it is large, and apply plasters convenient for this, to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	from the forcele
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forcele breaks many times before, near the shoulder, and the break is in three ways: either it is broken and separated into two parts, with one piece, and this is the easiest to reset; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is such that when the break is without a wound, you should have two assistants, one holding the shoulder where the forcele is broken, and the other extending the neck towards the affected part; then place the break evenly on your two hands, so that the form be as it should, and there be no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place a round pad of cloth or wool over the shoulder on the patient, and make it as large as necessary; then stretch and lift the forcele, and hold the pad with your hand, so that you can place the break evenly, as it should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder outwards, because it comes from below fully, then it is fitting that the patient lie often on his side, and place under the shoulder a medium pillow, and have the attendants press the shoulder downwards, until the bone of the shoulder be lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then treat the fracture with your two hands, and if you find any pieces displaced, you must split them; and draw the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any prominence, take one of your incisors; but place this instrument under the shoulder to prevent leakage.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, and is not misplaced, and be as wide as it ought to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and have two heads, as you see, and let one be broad, and the other narrow, as are the edges of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are assured of a hot abscess, close the wound, and if the opening is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, cover the wound with bandages and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses come around, I wrap them in rose oil and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The tightening of the bone, when it is affected by wounds and surgery, is that you apply the plaster of powder from the mill and egg yolk to the bone, then cover with light stops, and place a sphere underneath if needed; then take a very wide bandage about one palm in width, put the cloth doubled over the stops and the plaster. Take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, wrap it around that bandage so the ends hang down, and place the stick on the break, turn the bandage over the neck, under the stop, and between the healthy and affected areas; tighten each part, and when you see that the ties hold the break properly, and clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, reward it daily. When the ligaments loosen, release the restraint; have the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under the stop to raise the shoulder. This will alleviate the force of the injury by supporting the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless bad accidents occur, for up to twenty days. Then reapply the plaster if needed, keep it tight until restored; it is restored in most cases within twenty-eight days, and sooner for some individuals.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When it comes to the breaking of the shoulder or large crack, and cannot be felt by touch; arrange the parts according to the figure of the break, and reset them according to their natural form in all ways you can; then place on the bone flour mixed with abundant egg, and light plugs, and cover with a double cloth; then put over a broad and thin strip, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there is any movement in any part of the shoulder, use linen plug threads to secure it so that the strip remains evenly placed; and then tightly bind it with a large bandage, ensuring the strip does not move from its place, and examine the ligaments each day; whenever it settles, tighten the binding, and adjust the strip if it is out of place, and let the patient rest on their side; the shoulder will be restored in twenty or twenty-five days. And when these numbers are completed, release the bindings, and be sure, for it is not bone that sets quickly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone tends forward, and not over the heart, cut it out, and do as we have said in breaking the strong ligament to treat hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of breaking the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The foot is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it often breaks at the ankle.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends to one side, and the patient feels great pain, and has difficulty walking. Immediately, and by accident, they may vomit blood, and the movement in the broken bones becomes apparent, and everyone can see this well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies mostly on their back, and they place a cushion between the shoulders, then press the shoulders, and align the ribs of the two sides with your hands, and carefully position them so that the shape of the bone is as it should be; then apply plasters and ointments over the thin layer of salt or another light substance, wrap them in a cloth, and tie them around the broken bone to keep them from moving; turn the bandage round the back, adjust it appropriately, and secure the bandage every hour. If it becomes loose, tighten it; if it needs to be untied for corrosion or itching at the site, pain, or an abscess, act quickly, untie it, remove the plaster, and treat the area as in regular care; then reapply the plaster and keep it tight until healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the breaking of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The breaking of the ribs comes from force applied behind the shoulder and at the head inside, and they bend due to being overly flexible; one can feel it well upon inquiry around the area.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the restoration is to place the break equally, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply the plaster, and bandage it with a cloth if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the break of the ribs is inward, the patient feels great pain and a stabbing sensation, similar to tears, because the bone pierces the tissue; they wrinkle their face and immediately vomit much blood, which is a serious health issue. The elderly have used great skill in treating this.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if some say that it is fitting to administer foods that swell the belly, to drive away the colic.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make those who have not had an abscess come to one.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have had one, let them be cured.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And if any of you put cups on the shoulder to draw fluid strongly, and it seems reasonable; nonetheless, there is doubt that the cups will attract the superfluities to the shoulder due to the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And if any of you say that we should cover the shoulder with wet wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to make the duration equal, then it should be treated with the pleurisy cure, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure due to the bone where the tissue is torn, and there is doubt for the patient, it is necessary to incise above the rib of the broken costal cartilage, and put something under the instrument to protect the lung; then one must cut the bone, and draw lightly, and afterwards suture the two edges of the wound if it is large, and treat with plasters until he is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses continue, put wet cloths in rose oil and place them on the rib; and treat continually the rib as needed for the abscess, and let him lie over the side where it should be, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes the bones of the neck are broken, and rarely does it bend; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be cured or not, observe whether their hands are softened, swollen, and dead, and cannot move or extend, and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many respects, and if they can move and feel well when you hold and prick them, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient will recover if proper care is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will be cured or not, observe whether the pieces are softened, and if the accidents in the hands, and on the back due to wind and involuntary evacuation; and when it is touched on their abdomen, an involuntary evacuation follows.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is sooted on its back and he wishes to heal, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is fatal: he should not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this does not happen to him, it is the lighter matter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply it if there is a hot abscess, placing an oil of rose or egg yolk on it until it subsides; then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, and bind it with a bandage. Instruct the patient to rest; do not let him sleep on that part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone cracks, it must be covered with a cloth. Remove the bone, then join the two edges of the wound, if large, with stitches. Bind it with ointment promoting healing until it is healed. And if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow," you should hold your left handbag with your left hand and equalize it with your right hand as much as possible. Then apply the poultice and dressing if needed; bind it tightly. If there is a cracked bone, cut out the fragment, remove it, and treat the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the bone of the hip
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the bone of the hip is fractured, and it happens, there will be a slight alleviation in the head; and it becomes long, and inclines towards the buttocks, and causes great pain, swelling, and redness at the site.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above, as long as you are over the fractured area; and know which part is broken and its shape. If the break is only in the head, you must set it so that it is aligned, ensuring it takes on a natural figure.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is along its length, or it inclines inward, you must lie the patient on their stomach so that the restoration of the fracture can be aligned.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it even, put on the plaster, then put on a straw or rush mat, and hold the splint so that it does not move; and fill the space under the ribs, as the pieces should be even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side, or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if abscesses appear and swell, do not touch them until the abscesses are appeased, and put on what we have said before; then return to the restoration, and hold as it should be, if there is no adverse accident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires are those between the knife and the head of the shoulder, and if they are broken, you must restore them according to one of two methods: of which one is that you take a rod filled with moineen grain size, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And join the two heads of the links, and bend them upwards, and place the patient's broken arm on the rod; then throw the broken part of the arm onto the rod, until it reaches the armpit, with a piece of wood in between, then bend it over any heavy thing or let the attendants extend it downwards; then put the broken parts together evenly with both hands, so that the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you place the patient on his back, and tie the hand to the neck, then command two attendants such that one holds the part above the break with both hands, and the other holds the part below the link, extending each to their respective sections.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is stronger, hold the ligament below the break, and above the break, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the head of the shoulder, it is necessary that you place the ligament in the middle under the socket, and the other towards the knife, below the break; and likewise if the break is near the knife, you should place the ligament lightly, without strain, so that the break is equal both under the bone and under the knife; then set the break as it should be, and hold it, if no abscesses come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses come, you should not hold it tightly for seven days, and place a moistened cloth in oil of rose on the arm and under the shoulder or chest, until the abscesses are appeased; then hold it, and the way to hold it is that you apply the plaster over the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, holding tightly on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm is in a sling, unless something prevents it or the bone has not yet moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use stays, and place a larger and stronger stay above the break, with two fingers' breadth between each stay, and let each stay be so large that it passes the break three fingers' breadth from both sides; then pull on the stays as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the break, more forcefully but less by drawing away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the stays and the tension, as we have said, in the hour that you reset the broken limb, and you doubt whether the abscess is hot, let it remain free for seven days, as we have said; then examine each day the wound, to ensure that itching or swelling does not arise at the site, or that the granulations cannot come to the limb because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the treatment, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents happen, let the patient not be dislocated for more than three days or longer, and let the patient lie on his back, and place his hands on his stomach; and put under the shoulder a cushion full of evenly stuffed wool, and watch every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the tendons do not become soft; let the treatment proceed by the virtue of medicine, and give him the meat as we have placed before, in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; and when it begins to take hold, make it more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is custom that the shoulder and the leg should be repositioned within forty days from the beginning; then one must reset them and administer baths and ointments to treat them.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and contracted, it must remain to be untied for one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fasciculus," of which one is small and is that which surrounds the pouch; and the other is large, and is that which is beneath, opposite the small finger; by chance the large fasciculus may be broken alone, or the small one, and by chance both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small fasciculus is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is poor, and worse than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is the small fragile bone that is broken only, then it should be extended gently and placed evenly.
