Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone, you should extend it more forcefully; and place it on the bench, and hold the pouch of your hand higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others. And let the patient cross his limbs over himself, and the bench in front higher so the patient does not suffer any labor; then stretch your ministers' arms under your hand or to the side, and another minister above the other part.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then place the bones evenly, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the break into pieces, place each piece in its place. And if there is any detached part that cannot be grasped and restored to its place, cut it out, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And when using the blade for wounds, I spoke of it in the singular chapter; so take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if during the beginning of the restoration abscesses appear, glue the bandage made of rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; and tie the bandage tightly enough so that the abscesses are alleviated.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerote, and apply the plaster of the powder from the mill mixed with abundant egg, then place the plasters, and let the blade plasters be tied more tightly, and a bit wider than the others; and know that there should be six plasters or arms in various positions: whether the blade is in one of the bones, or two. Bind more tightly above the blade than elsewhere, and loosen less as the days pass, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages above the blade be soft and moist, and not hard nor harsh; and let the threads from which they are made be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, it is necessary that you rinse the member with warm water until the itching is soothed; and let the member rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then reapply the binding. If the ligaments have softened and the bones displaced, address as necessary.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you notice that the swelling cannot come to the member, because it is too tight, it is necessary that you loosen it a little, and let it be for a few days, until the swelling subsides, and then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, do not let him lie dislocated for up to twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or about the neck, then turn him and place his hands on his neck, and let his neck be level, and guard against movement and disturbance, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty days or in thirty-five, and by chance in twenty, according to the mixtures and compositions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers, there are few fractures, and there often comes much swelling.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the sole of the hand is broken or swollen, the patient should place his hand straight in front of him with the palm facing down; then have the assistants extend the broken bones and align the joints so they are properly joined; apply the plaster and stopes if no abscesses occur, and then place a bandage according to the size of the hand; and let it be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the bone of the sole between the toes, make a sphere of bandages, and instruct the patient to hold it on his injured sole; and then wrap with a long strip of cloth, and let it be an istle of hemp wool as large as the palm of the hand, and wrap it so as is fitting.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the foot, it is fitting that you place one istle above and another below on the sole, so that the hand be open and straight, then tie tightly around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the toes.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to any of our toes, if it is displaced, set it equal, as is fitting; and wrap it with the sole, and if you see, place a small straight istle to lift the fracture and prevent movement; and if the fracture is on other toes, such as in the index or one of the others, set it equal, and tie with the healthy toe that follows; or you may tie them all together, keeping them from moving, or place a patch like a pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of hot abscesses, and help those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the thigh is often broken, and one can see this when it turns front and back; and its restoration consists in tying above the break and below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on their side, then each minister extends their bandage to their respective part evenly; and this is when the break is placed on the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, place one bandage against the knife, and the other bandage below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then place the bandages below the knee, and the extension downwards; then set the bone equally with both hands, so that it is according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster and the bandage, unless abscesses appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside first then return to your work and treatment; the incision is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap the broken bone with a double bandage of two or three layers, and let any excess remain, then turn the leg until the heel touches the root of the toes, and place a long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee joint, and let the end of the thread appear above; then turn back to the leg and thigh with the bandage, and place strips over the broken bone; fill the space between the thigh and the leg with soft cloth to ensure equal pressure, then begin to tie three or four turns around the broken bone; as you go further from the broken bone, tie it less tightly; then adjust the two ends of the thread that you placed between the thigh and the leg, and place three strips above them, then return below to the end of the thread until you reach the foot; tighten so that it does not move in its place, then leave it as is, ensuring no abscess or swelling occurs elsewhere.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, release it, and set what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it must be washed if one can; and if one cannot, it must cut the flesh, and draw out the force; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the thigh broken thus one sets it with stakes, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, in the restoration thus performed, the patient does not complain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thigh is restored in one day, or somewhat less or somewhat more, according to the多样性 of constitution。
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the groove of the knee there is little breakage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is not merely a crack or hole, but comes about from any wound, and feels like a deep wound.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that you place equal wax on its ends until they are firmly joined; then apply the plaster, and put a round stick if you need it, and hold it as necessary. Afterward, re-establish all the arrangements we have said for other fractures, such as hot abscesses and similar conditions; apply what is suitable for each condition until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by its proper name "moustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and it breaks altogether as it does in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is equally so, and the works are all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then turn the leg in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the fine bone is broken, then turn it forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then there is great pain, and one can see it clearly; and turn it back.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply extension, and set it equal, and bind the straps equally; but in any case, if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the extension should be less and more gentle; and lighten according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed all your work, take two pieces of woven willow that extend the length of the leg from the knee downward on both sides, then wrap them in two layers with one bandage over and under, and tie them in the middle. At this point, neither leg can decline to the right nor to the left, and thus it is well; no long pieces of willow are administered into the leg, and it is placed for guarding against movement. This is properly done at a fracture or where there is a wound; each day move the leg to see if there is any abscess or other accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones at the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	A the foot no break comes, but in the bones of the foot a break comes sometimes and in the toes much more, and there is strength only with many conditions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if a break comes in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones sticking out one over the other, set the patient's foot on the ground as if it wanted to walk, and then place your foot on its foot where the bones are raised, pressing them until they return to their places; then put the plaster and ointment on, and place a small board with two stones under the sole of the foot, then bind it properly. After you have wrapped it tightly with bandages and other things you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers; then put on each broken finger a splint according to its length, and let it be somewhat wider, then put under the foot that block which I have said, and bind it appropriately; and if there are two or three or more broken ones, place on each finger a splint according to its quantity, wrapped in one linen cloth, and bind the block under the sole of the foot; and let it be placed above the top of the block behind the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said for the other broken bones, as we have said; and support each accident as it requires.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone at the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's hand is broken by nature, make her sit with her arm extended, then incline it toward the back part, and keep her supported behind; then fill the space in the woman's body with cotton, making it as large as the bone; then remove the woman and slowly elevate the back, so that the cotton comes to the entrance of the body, and the bone returns with the bone; and when she wants to urinate, take out the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days or more: thus will be restored the break, and if you want, take a bladder from a lamb, tie a string at the opening, and fill the entire bladder inside; then blow into the string forcefully, so that the bladder is inflated within: the body will return the break; then fill it with cotton and leave it for some days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand of the man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these nearby fractures are not hidden from him who applies his study and understanding, and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fractures signify in many dispositions the right way of restoration: understand them accordingly.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the thigh, when it is broken, take a goose's jaw and insert the thigh into it; then wrap it tightly with bandages, and let it be for three days or longer, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is large, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade or similar, to be healed now, as our treatments indicate.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is sound, treat it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then proceed to restore the damage at that same hour or on that day, unless an abscess develops.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if an abscess develops, delay the restoration until the next new day, as long as the abscess is pacified. Do not touch it on the third day or the fourth, for you would cause evil accidents to arise.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the uncovered shoulder, it is necessary to place it gently with your hands, extending it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not provided to make it equal with your hands, use an instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight long prongs, and its width is according to the size of the wound; and for this, you need a splint that can be soaked in three or four parts, depending on what it needs for each treatment of a broken bone; and let it be round and slightly thick, so it does not bend under compression on the limb during your work, and let it be flat in front, and wide at the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche," which means that the curved heads of the shoulder must be placed on the top of the visible bone; and strike once, so that it returns, and let them be level against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instruments cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instrument can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone, as we have said, with a suitable instrument cut, using either an incisor or a soiree, to your power; then retain what remains in the bone by hardness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so while it is in its place, then wet a cloth in wine from a grape must, and properly if it is fresh; and do not put any ointment or other thing on the wound that it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer leeches when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the covering all around, according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not compressed with the breakage; and many times fools have done this and caused illness or death or corruption in the patient at least once; and let the compressions be softer and more gentle than other breakages.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that some evil accident may occur, as we have said, and you find pain at the site, it is not fitting to put on leeches; but wrap around, instead of leeches, cloths tightly, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days the wound inking at the wound, remove what you have put on for all wine, and apply healing ointment for wounds, as tetralfarmacion and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is set and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb must be aligned in such a manner that the wound heals smoothly and gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if many days pass and the wound does not close further, know that there are small bone fragments, for which you must clean the wound with a tent, and remove all these detached pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the shoulder, or any other form of corruption, it must be treated, according to what is stated in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opened in the same limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and others like them in the large limbs, do not reduce it, for many times death comes from it, but leave it until it rots; by chance it may fall out by itself after 20 or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of blisters that come over the scalding
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Many times after the scalding, blisters come, especially when it is near the joint. It is a sad sight to see the figure of the limb; and by chance it cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, take heed that if the joint is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and shellac, acacia, and similar others, whichever of these you find or all together, and prepare them with styptic wine or with plenty of egg or with oil; place them on the knot in stoppered vessels, and bind well, not releasing by hand for several days; then remove it, and begin another until the knots are removed; or you may bind over a well-made piece of lint; for the property of linen is that it removes all swellings above the limbs; and if the knot has become as hard as stone and must be removed, cover with a poultice and let the excess appear; or you may have it shaved until it is removed, and cure until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which is weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored and remains after the member is weak and subtle, it happens for much reason: one of which is because it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and the nourishments could not come to the member; or due to too much swelling; or from too great movements, not at their proper time; or because there is little blood in the body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you make the patient eat and strengthen the body until the flesh multiplies in him; and you give him baths, and grant him joy and pleasure; then apply ointment to the member, so that the ointment draws towards the great nourishment, and frequently wash it with hot water until the nourishment comes to the member; and return to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the limb twisted after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after recovery, and the broken bones are exposed, and the shape of the limb is ugly, all in all, it does not impair its natural function: one should not believe those fools who say that one must break the limb completely anew; many such foolish acts have been done in our land; these works are blamed, and they bring great harms, and by chance, death; altogether, if the swelling and pain are fresh, it is necessary to apply hot water, or to cook herbs that soften, such as leaves of vismarvel, roots, and marjoram, and similar medicines; then apply a soothing plaster, well made, and you take the muscilage of vismarvel, and mix it with tallow or olive oil, and apply it on top; or you take fatty figs, grind them with colon flour, and use similar medicines that reduce swelling suddenly.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the nodation is removed to be rubbed continuously and for a long time with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And move the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is hardened like stone and it needs to be removed with iron, then it should be cut up to the bone with a sharp incisor gently; and apply careful attention and skill in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to someone, it is fitting now to reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Since one delays, the shoulder swells, and by chance if it is reset when swollen; because this is not fitting to move it while swollen: many times it brings on spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient rest, until the abscesses are healed; then arise the limb in warm oil, and cure each part as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the shoulder to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Often the jaws are dislocated sideways, and the dislocations on both sides occur in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their places and made somewhat softer; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the ear, and block the saliva from the mouth so he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, wrapping his tongue with the word.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it often returns to place through natural means.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if the dislocation is complete and thorough, you must reset it quickly without delay; and in such a manner that the attendant holds the patient's head, and places some moistened cloths from one of his hands at the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation involves both sides; and the other hand should support evenly. Instruct the patient to soften and move his jaws in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And you place the joint evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to bring back, even if it is the two mandibles together, then soak them in hot water and oil, and gently reset them; do not press hard when resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back evenly, and the patient's mouth closes well, then apply a moist dressing in a paste made of rose oil and wax. Then tie it loosely with soft threads. Let the patient sleep on their back, with their head between two cushions so that it cannot move left or right, nor try to chew. Instead, give them light food until the pain is gone, and secure the mandibles; then let him eat lightly as he wishes, without forcing his mouth open for eating and drinking, until the mandible is well set and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandible bones cannot be reset to place within an hour and are not fully returned to their sockets, then fevers and stiffness become accustomed, and by chance there may be intestinal paralysis, and by chance vomiting of black bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is fatal; many times those who suffer from it die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the forceps
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot dislocate the lower rib within the continuation of the bone and is only dislocated once at the fracture, and one can feel this.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies often on their back and stretches out their arms. Then press the bone firmly to your palm, and it will return; thereafter apply the plaster and bandage, and tighten it. The head near the cut cannot be dislocated; if only slightly, and if it is dislocated once, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed. Thus, the head of the shoulder is brought back when it is displaced from its socket.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: the first is when it dislocates at the socket's bottom; and the second is at the back of the pit; and by chance it dislocates above, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates from below towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, as it jumps quickly in them; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with strength and returns with strength.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men through a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated for this reason.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must test it thoroughly until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known the dislocation when it goes toward the socket, and you make a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a clear difference between them; and you will find a basin at the head of the shoulder, and beneath the socket at the toucher the head of the shoulder, as if it were an eye; and the sick one cannot bring its hand to its nose, nor move by any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, for you find it clearly at the toucher; and this manner of dislocation is not easy to reset when it is new, or when the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places his palms underneath the armpit, and displaces the joint with force upwards to its place; and the minister lifts his hand and extends it upwards, then puts it under; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said by hand a few days later, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and the minister should apply soothing and relaxing applications, such as a decoction of althea, fenugreek, and marigold in water, and apply them. Then the patient's back should be shaved, and a piece of woolen cloth, neither too soft nor too hard, should be placed under the armpit; then place the patient's heel on the cloth, and lift the shoulder blade properly, and pull the patient's hand upwards; and another minister should hold the patient's head downwards so that it does not move. This shoulder will return to its proper position immediately, and if you find it necessary to reset it in this manner: then make sure a person larger than the patient is present; and place them upright against the side, and insert the shoulder under the armpit of the patient, and lift the armpit upwards so that the patient hangs from the arm; and another minister should pull the patient's hand downwards towards the abdomen.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he may add something heavy to him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the dislocation is also reduced in another manner: and it is such that one sticks a long poker into the ground, where the head of the shoulder should be as round as a pelt, neither too large nor too small; then it is placed under the patient, but it has a sleeve at the top, and the patient's arm should be extended downward from another direction firmly; and the joint will return to its place quickly. And if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, do this treatment: take a poker two arm lengths long and four fingers wide, which has a head round enough to enter perfectly under the armpit, according to this form.
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then bind above the head of the rod under, so that the rod does not bruise the patient, then place it under the armpit; and stretch out your arm above the long rod, and bind the shoulder to the rod, and the arm to the head of the hand, then place the arm on a step of a ladder wide, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging from another side: the joint will now recover gradually.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is done, in whatever manner that may be, you must place under the armpit a pad of wool equal, then apply the plaster mixed with powder of grindstone, with incense and egg yolk, over all the shoulder and around, then remove the pad accordingly, and turn the bandage over the plaster, and wrap the hand at its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be eaten little, so that the limb becomes strengthened, for it will heal faster; and thereafter eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture or for another reason, it must be treated with three cauteries at intervals, as is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it dislocates after 7 days, and the joint does not hold and cannot lift the arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint was never set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations in the hip and breasts, or behind, are caused by impulse and extension of hands; and they are treated until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing there is pain in the limb, and delay with movement, the patient should take bath many times until that pain subsides, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; and it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind. The dislocation is not replied to, for one can see it clearly and feel it well; and it is dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the diseased part with the healthy one, you must see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And the joint is stiff, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it as abscesses form and come to head. For if abscesses form and come to head, it would be grievous to bring it back; and by chance it cannot be brought back entirely, especially when it is at the rear. It is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and by chance it leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it can be reset, that you extend its hand with both your hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands on either side of the cut, front and back, and apply pressure to the joint at its edges or at the root of its palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and fixes the root of the palm cut which is displaced.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not wish to return to its place, administer strong extension; and two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with their hands, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm in all directions, then wrap it tightly in a double long and wide cloth; and when the minister joins the joint to his hand, anoint with any oil to soften the joint, then form the joint properly until it returns; and when it is in its place, put on a dry plaster with egg yolk, and hold the arm at the neck of the patient, and let it lie for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly set in its place, untie the bandage and leave it off; and if you see that the joint does not fit well, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and leave them on for some days, until it is firmly set; then untie it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if it feels injured after the reset of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and gently rub it, pressing until it is relieved; or you can place a fat sheep tallow on the joint for one day and one night, then remove it and let the plaster in. When it sweats, thoroughly rub the joint, then put the tallow back on, and let it soak in the bath; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, place heated moist horse fat with butter on it, then apply it; it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand becomes more severe, and the return is light, less than other joints. Whenever it is dislocated, one must reset it quickly, within the hour it became dislocated, just as the joint swells or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the resetting is as follows: you place the injured hand on a table, extend the fingers of the helper's hand, and position their palm equally so that it touches the appearance of the joint. Hold until it returns to its proper place. You must ensure it is correctly set; then, place the back of the injured hand on the table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's back of his hand on the table, and the attendant place his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	And if it returns now, that is well. If not, apply a plaster to calm the abscess and let it be so until it begins again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, the joint remains twisted; and it does no harm to the patient as long as the hand is softened, and cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerve is cut, or the artery; there is no other means of treating it except by cauterizing near the case, and by chance nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put on the plaster that we have said, then bind it and let it be 5 days, then unbind it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is any swelling, apply hot liquid grease and rub it until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated in any direction, sometimes at the back of the palm or the palm's center; then straighten the finger, and hold the dislocation with your fingers until it returns to place. Then support the thumb of the finger, and push it towards the part where it is disjoined; and let it be 2 days, and then make it equal on that day; and do not bind it as we have said, and unbind it daily, and allow it to move, and rebind it at night; and do this often until it is tightly set. If it is dislocated in the palm of the hand, do so as you did before until it heals. Do the same if it is dislocated in any other part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation of the shoulder blade of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no point in treating it, as death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the vomit leaps without desire, neither can it be held, and often they soften some limb, or both hips, or both arms. And often the shoulder blade changes in four parts; that which changes at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you reward if the gilbositez came from childhood: there is no cure nor healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment with grand words say they have no real benefit in all cases; but I have abbreviated it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gilbositeit that comes before the pis, there is no health; and so it is with that which comes directly into two sides, and one cannot cure it except that which comes to the back, as I say. And it is that the patient be stretched evenly on his back, and have a strain beneath him, that he does not stiffen; then stick a coal at the head in the ground firmly, and another at the feet, and tie one string under the armpits of the patient, and the other at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two ministers know the strings, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two coals; and may their hands be well closed, the coal as we have said, and the martyr place his palms on the spine firmly until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return through this cure, take a board of three spans long, place it under the wall, and if the patient is on their side, put the head of the board under the wall, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and have the patient's feet on the other head of the board, and press well until it returns to its place; and if you see, do so at the wheel that turns by hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you place two coals in the head of the patient's arm with one hand, and near the feet with the other, and between each coal, underneath and above, place a palm of long spice; and in each coal, let there be a hole, or where the wheel runs, and let the coals be firmly set in the ground so they do not move; and between each two coals, have one turning coal on which the thread turns, and have two small coals of a palm's length for turning the wheel; and then tie the thread that is among the spindles to the wheel near the head, and the other thread near the feet to the other wheel, and each attendant turns their wheel with the thread, and the master keeps the spine level as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when they are equal, apply a desiccative plaster with abundant egg, and then the stoppers, and then place a piece of three long fingers of linen that purifies the muscle from fatiness and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and use the patient for gradual healing until they are healed; and if any thing comes at the end of the healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the poultice that we have mentioned before; and sometimes one administers a piece of flax, and sometimes the appearance in the rear spine of the back indicates dislocation; and this is the bone that appears, so one must not presume anything: by chance it might bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and the joints of the shoulder come about only from dislocations, not in the same way as other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: internally and externally, in front and behind; more internally it is more so, and less so in front and behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of a dislocation internally is that when one joins the injured leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and more clearly the injured knee appears larger than the healthy one, and the injured knee cannot bend at all; this is because the head of the femur comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it happens is that these accidents are contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him to whom these happen in advance are that his leg is well positioned; nevertheless, he cannot bend his knee without pain, and if one tries to make him walk, he cannot do so and retains his urine, and swells his ankle, and when he goes, he passes over his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him to whom these happen later are that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is at the site below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment for this resemblance of dislocation is that you reward if the dislocation is old, and it remains in its position, then there is no need for any treatment; and it must not have any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that which concerns the fresh dislocation, and this is of four kinds of dislocation, you must hasten to turn the joint, and stretch it inside and outside, and move it right and left; by chance it will return, and has no need of further care.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong assistant, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or at the place where it is tied above the knee; and another assistant extend his hand above in such a way that he places his hands under its armpits, then tighten it with a bandage around the thigh; and another holds the head of the injured person; and they extend both upwards and downwards at once, so that the patient is lifted from the ground at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for the four similarities, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not so, it is necessary to treat with its similarity. If the dislocation is in the shoulder blade, you must soothe the patient on his healthy side, then place the bandage at the root of the thigh, and below the angle, then position the bandage upwards towards the angle and the forcelet; then have another minister grasp his arms, and embrace the large muscle of the affected thigh, and extend it firmly: it will now return to its place; and this method of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in this manner as we have said, it is necessary that you bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong bandage above the ankles and knees, and let the affected leg be extended twice as much as the other; then hang it from the top of a stake, and extend its arms long on either side. Then command the minister to embrace the top of the thigh, and have another minister hanging along with the patient, who firmly embraces the thigh, for the joint is now returning quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are at fault, the patient lies down, as we have said in that which has gilbositeit, and extract the vein properly above the bad leg, and also on the ankle; then place two torches, one at the head and the other at the foot, then insert the torch between the thighs of the bad limb in the form; and plant moist cloths around, so that it does not blister the bad limb, then extend each minister towards him, and the eyes put equal to his hand the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	And if it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	And if not, place it on the table and press it as we have said in the gilbositeit, and let the patient lie on the good side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is forward, it must be stretched the bad leg quickly, and according to what I have said; and place the palm of the hand above the bad knee, then press with the other hand, stretching downward toward the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.
