And if the dislocation is to the side, it must not be stretched downward or lifted from the ground, but rather placed as if the hip were dislocated to the side, as we have said in the躺卧两髋关节部分; and place it on its side, with the ligament stretched as we said before, and press on the joint at the table; it will be right when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then adjust the thighs, apply the plaster, and secure with a bandage so that the hips do not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then release it and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, secure as before and leave it for three days; then release it, and allow it to heal properly until the limbs are strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee can be dislocated in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not settle against the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his thigh, and put his foot on yours; then take his knee with your palms, and pull gently between your hands, and bend the two sides of the knee firmly; and have other ministers extend his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that his leg settles lightly against the thigh; and apply the plaster, and warm the leg at the thigh, and tie them tightly for three or four days, then release the bindings; and do not allow the patient to move much until the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not straight, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankle is sometimes injured, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and displaced forward to the part where it is dislocated: the displacement is slight, and one should gently extend it with their hands when it is only injured.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, you must seat the patient upright, and have the attendants hold him by the leg above the ankle. Then pull the foot toward your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, then extend it upward, and firmly place the foot in position. Do this twice as we have said, pulling and stretching the foot; if it returns, that is well; if not, restart the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and drive a stake firmly into the earth between his thighs, binding him tightly with bandages so as not to displace the patient. Then have the attendants hold his thigh, and others extend the foot by their hands or at the ankle, securing it above the foot's neck; then equally stretch each attendant, and the stake should be fastened between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when it is extended; then place your fingers on either side of the dislocation with your hands, and have others hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will quickly return to its proper position.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is in place, put the plaster and stops on it, then draw out the splint, and bind the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves that are behind the ankle, so that the ties are not too tight; then let it be for two or three days, and as the ties loosen, remove the splint; then unbind at the third or fourth day, and defend the patient from walking for four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not safety that he will dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses arise, you must relieve them as we have said elsewhere until they are healed.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When they are dislocated, you must beautifully extend them with effort, and this is a light matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any notch of the back of the foot, you must seat the patient on a firm bench or on a II. table completely straight, and place his foot on what stands out from these joints, then press firmly on his foot until it returns; and when it is equal and nothing stands out, put a shoulder-blade under the sole of the foot, then hold firmly, and leave for three days, then release; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and you see it healing, many times the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not used it long, and if you are not all-wise and merciful and slow; and use at the beginning soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and leave the patient to God if you see no hope of recovery; and when you see hope, now reset the limb to its place as the hot abscesses begin to subside; and when the limb is in place, administer soothing remedies for hot abscesses, and cure the wound as it should be with drying ointments; and if there is a fracture with small broken bones, remove them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and guard against entering the way of fear according to what I have said, for this will bring you trouble according to your Creator, and because of the knowledge that arms and bodies should have.
Amen	Amen
